The author of this book completed it for you, my sons, as a part of the science of medicine in its entirety and has reached the goal within it through clarity and explanation. I saw that I should complete it with this chapter which is a part of the work by hand.
Because the art of surgery is non-existent in our land and at our time, almost to the point where its knowledge is not studied and its influence ceases. And what remained of it was only slight sketches in the books of the ancients, which were blurred by the passage of time and the mistakes and confusion that occurred until its meaning was lost and its benefit was delayed.
So I saw that I should revivify it and compile this chapter in the manner of explanation and illustration, and come with the forms of surgical instruments and all the tools of work as they are necessary for clarity and to facilitate what is required.
And the reason why there is no skilled surgeon in our time because the art of medicine is long and it is necessary for its practitioner to be familiar beforehand with the science of anatomy which Galen described. Until he stands on the benefits of the organs and their functions, and how they are connected and disconnected, and knows the bones, nerves, muscles, and their numbers, exits, and blood vessels and tendons and where their exits are.
Therefore, Albucasis said that physicians are many by name but few in reality and especially in the art of surgery, and we have mentioned some aspects of this in the introduction to this book.
Because he who is not knowledgeable about what we have mentioned in anatomy may fall into error and kill people with it, just as I have seen many who pretend to know this science without knowledge or understanding.
And that is because I saw a ignorant doctor who cut into a goiter in a woman's neck, and he severed some of the neck's ligaments so the woman's blood flowed until she fell dead at his feet.
I saw a doctor who extracted a stone from a man who had been stabbed in the back and the stone was large so he broke it out with a piece of bladder membrane. The man died after about three days, and I was summoned to extract it, so I saw the stone and the patient's condition as I had predicted.
I saw another doctor who was working with some of our town's notables in medicine.
Then an incident occurred with a young man who had a fracture in his leg near the ankle, along with a wound. The doctor hastened to it without knowledge and applied the splint to the wound with bands and ligatures tightly, leaving no room for the wound to breathe.
Then he let him follow his desires, then left him for a few days and ordered him not to remove the bandage until his leg and foot had swollen and was on the verge of death.
Then I was summoned to him, and I hastened to remove the bandage. He gained relief from his pain and sat up from his distress, but the damage had already become severe in the limb, and I was unable to restore it.
So the damage continued to progress in the limb until he died.
I saw another doctor who treated a cancerous tumor, and it ulcerated after some days until his patient's swelling grew, that is, if the cancer was pure from black bile, then one should not apply iron to it at all.
Unless it is in an organ that can tolerate its removal.
And so, my sons, you should know that the practice of medicine is divided into two parts: one that accompanies safety and one that brings harm in most cases.
And I have warned about every place where this book's practice brings danger and fear, so you should beware of it and reject it.
Unless the ignorant one finds the way to speak and cut, take hold of yourselves with firmness and self-control, and treat your patients with kindness and reassurance.
And use the best route leading to safety and the praised outcome, and overcome the serious and difficult diseases.
And purify yourselves from what you fear may corrupt your faith and your worldly and otherworldly affairs, for this is the greatest blessing for your souls and elevated in both worlds and hereafter for your destinies.
For Galen said in some of his counsels: Do not cure a bad disease, and call yourselves bad doctors.
And this treatise has been divided into three doors.
The first door.
In fire and in acute medicine, a summary of the art from the beginning to the end, and illustrations of the instruments and equipment needed for manual work.
The second door.
In surgery, the treatment of wounds, bloodletting, cupping, and phlebotomy, and extracting arrows and similar things, a summary in order with illustrations of the instruments.
The third door.
In setting fractures, removing splints, and treating ulcers and similar things, a summary in order from beginning to end with illustrations of the instruments.
The first door.
About fire.
And before we mention the use of it, we should mention its benefits and drawbacks, and in what temperament it is used.
For I say that the discussion of the benefits and drawbacks of fire is a long and detailed knowledge, and a hidden secret, which some wise men have discussed.
And they disagreed about it, and I have only briefly mentioned their words, out of fear of prolonging the discussion.
For I say that fire is beneficial in general to every bad temperament, whether it is with matter or without matter, except for two temperaments: the fiery temperament without matter and the dry temperament without matter.
As for the dry temperament with matter, they have differed in that some say that it is beneficial and others say that it is contrary to that, saying that it does not suit a disease that comes from heat and dryness because the nature of fire is heat and dryness.
And it is possible to treat a hot and dry disease with a hot and dry medicine, and he who says contrary to that says that the fire can be effective in treating a hot and dry disease that occurs in human bodies. Because when you mix the moisture of the human body with the temperament of fire, it cools the human body down.
And I say so because experience has revealed it to me on many occasions, but one should not assume that without having thoroughly studied and learned about the matter. And he based himself on the difference in temperaments of people, and their diseases, and their causes, symptoms, and durations.
And as for the other temperaments, there is no fear of them, and especially not the cold and moist diseases, upon which all physicians have agreed and have not disagreed about the effectiveness of fire in treating them.
And know, my sons, that one who excels in treating with fire and values it over burning medicine because fire is a single substance whose action is confined to the part where it is applied and does not harm another connected part except slightly.
And the burning medicine may exceed its action to other parts and perhaps cause a disease in another part that is difficult to treat, or even be fatal; whereas fire, by virtue of its nobility and excellence, does not do so except if it is excessive.
And this has been revealed to us through experience, after a long period of service and care in the craft, and by standing on the truths of the matter.
And therefore I have spared you from a long speech, but if it were not fitting for this book of mine, I would have explained to you in the fire a mysterious secret and its manner of action in the bodies, and how it rejects diseases with philosophical and demonstrative language that would clarify your understanding.
Know that my sons that they have disagreed on the time when it is proper to do a c-section and they have considered best the spring season.
And I say that a c-section can be done at any time, for the harm caused by delay is absorbed by the benefit brought about by the c-section. And especially if the c-section is necessary for a serious and imminent danger that cannot be delayed, lest it result in greater harm than the initial harm caused by delay.
And do not let your minds, my sons, be swayed by the ignorant and inexperienced doctors who think that a c-section is only necessary when there is no possibility of recovery from an illness and it will only result in death.
And do not think that the c-section is only a means of administering medicine to alleviate the mood and dry up the humors that are the cause of the pain.
Unless the c-section surpasses medicine in terms of rapid success, strong action, and intense effect.
And it is possible that the illness may return at some time, depending on the patient's temperament and their ability to resist it, as well as the accumulation of humors in their body and neglecting themselves by indulging in their desires and similar causes.
May God forbid that the illness for which a c-section is performed be a trivial one and affecting a small area with minimal humors and moisture. Like an excision of a tooth from the pain, and similar cases, it is possible that the pain will not return in such cases and this would be the best.
And as for the saying of the common people that a c-section is the last resort, it is a true saying not going against what they claim because they believe that there is no treatment effective by medicine or otherwise after a c-section has taken place and this is unlike other cases.
And indeed the meaning of "Innama" is that whenever we use various treatments for a disease and those treatments do not benefit, then we use what remains as a remedy, so from here the outcome is "Innama" the last treatment. Not according to the opinion of the common people and many ignorant doctors.
And the ancients mentioned that the k朝 (last resort) with gold is better than the k朝 with iron, and they said this because of the moderation of gold and its noble essence, and they said it does not harm the place of the k朝; it is not at all like that.
For I have tried that and found it to be the case, for it does this in some bodies rather than others, and the k朝 with it is better and more excellent than iron as they said; except that if you protect the material from fire using gold, you will not know when to stop at the quantity of gold you desire because of its redness.
And because it hastens towards cold and if you add more to the fever it melts in fire, and we found the craftsman busy with that; therefore the k朝 with iron is faster and closer to the truth for work, God willing.
And I have organized this book on the k朝 into chapters from head to foot in order to make it easy for the student to find what he wants, God willing.
The First Chapter.
On the K朝 of the Head: One Method.
This k朝 is effective against the oppression of moisture and cold on the brain, which are the cause of headaches, frequent vomiting from the head to the direction of the eyes and ears, excessive sleep, toothache, and sore throat. In general, this k朝 is beneficial for every disease that arises from cold, such as apoplexy, epilepsy, and numbness, and other similar diseases.
Image of this kind: first, instruct the patient to take the gentle and purified medicine for the head three nights or four according to what is required by the patient's strength, age, and habit.
Then instruct him to shave his head with a razor, then seat him in front of you, reclining and placing his hands on his chest.
Then place the tip of your finger on the tip of his nose between his eyes, and where the middle phalanx of your finger ends, mark that spot with a dot.
Then take the ointment.
If you have exposed a part of the skull equal to the space between two scales or equal to a grain of barley, lift your hand and if not, then retract your hand with the same razor or another one if it is cold. Until you see the bone as I mentioned to you, then take something of salt, dissolve it in water, soak a piece of linen in it, and put it on the spot, and leave it for three days.
Then wrap it with a wet linen soaked in lard, and leave it on him until the scab falls off like ash from fire, then treat it with the quadruple ointment until he recovers if God wills.
And they said that an open wound, the more it remains open, the better and more effective it is.
And some of them said that the skin should be sewn onto the bone, and hold the ointment until some thickness of the bone is burned, then remove what has been burned from the bone, and treat it.
And others said that it is necessary to apply the caustic substance until it has a strong effect on the bone, so that it falls off like a scale or a small piece of bark, and they claimed that this substance purifies the head from that spot and leaves the wound open for a long time.
Then he treats until it heals, and I do not see these two types of ulcers anywhere else except in some people on the way of holes and leaving it with me. If that is the case, then the head swells when its natural connection is severed as we have seen in all other limbs.
And especially when the patient's head is weak by nature and I use the first type of ulcers, it works well with me and I work with it accordingly, if Allah wills.
The second chapter.
Also in the head.
If an inflammation occurs in the head, and it becomes chronic and persists in the patient, and I have tried applying poultices, fomentations, plasters, dressings, and bandages, especially if he has had only one ulcer as we described, and nothing has benefited him from that, then look. If the patient's head is naturally strong and not weak, and he finds a severe ulcer, then I cover another ulcer above it slightly. Then I cover all the bones of his head with an ulcer until the thickness of the skin goes away and the bone condition we described is revealed. And I cover an ulcer in the back of his head, at the spot known as the hatchet, and ease off your hand here so that you do not reveal the bone, because the patient will find it very painful, unlike the pain of all other ulcers on the head; and I will mention this ulcer in its place.
And the covering that covers the horns of the head and its back should be softer than the one that covers the middle of the head, and this is its shape.
The third chapter.
Also in the femur that is not chronic.
If inflammation occurs in the skull with a headache and dizziness, and the pain extends to the eye, then the patient relieves himself with purgatives for the head and applies all the treatment I mentioned earlier; if that does not work, then the ulcer is on two sides. If it is necessary to treat by a hot medication and melted oil, or by iron.
If it is necessary to treat by hot medication, it is that you take a piece of garlic, and scrape it, and cut its edges from both sides, then split the place of pain on the cheek with a broad knife until there is a space under the skin which can accommodate the garlic.
He inserts it under the skin until it disappears, then tightens it with a firm grip and leaves it for as long as fifteen hours, then releases it and takes out the garlic, leaving the wound two or three days before removing.
On it, anoint with a thread soaked in fat until the place becomes numb, then treat it with ointment until it heals if God wills, and if you wish, do that with some of the hot medicines I mentioned in chapter 18 of the hot medicines.
And as for treating it by iron, on this manner: make the instrument which is shown thus:.
And it is called the Somanian instrument because its head resembles a small peg with some wrapping, and in the middle of it there is a small groove.
Then you put it on the place of pain, and grasp your hand tightly while turning the iron a little by little, and what is burnt from the thickness of the skin will be about half. And raise your hand so that you don't burn the artery that is below, and bleeding occurs, then take a thread in salt water and put it on the place and leave it for three days. Then anoint the thread with fat, and treat it with ointment until it heals if God wills.
And if you wish, cut this ligature with the sharp edge that comes from the instrument and keep it away from cutting the artery in this ligature especially.
The Fourth Chapter.
Concerning Chronic Haemorrhoids.
If you treated the piles with what we have mentioned as treatment beforehand and with what we have mentioned in the division of diseases, and the treatment did not succeed, and I saw from the cause that it is not capable of being cured by what we have mentioned first, either through medicine or fire. Then it is necessary to guard the skin until it becomes white, after you have learned where the pain is by its length in a straight line of half an inch or so, and leave your hand once and pull it back until it cuts the artery and reaches towards the bone.
Unless you take care to separate the jawbone which moves when chewing, and burn or sever the muscle or nerve controlling it, so that contraction occurs.
And be on guard for bleeding from the artery which you have cut, as there is fear of its cutting. Especially not for one who does not know what to do and has not been tried and tested, and has left the first attempt.
And the treatment of bleeding from the artery will be mentioned in its place in this book, God willing. If you see from the cause that it cannot be cured by this cauterization.
And if you see the patient's body obstructed, apply cauterization in the middle of the head as we have described and treat the wound until it heals, God willing.
And if you wish, use the cauterization that we mentioned in the chapter on arresting blood flow with the double-edged knife, for it is a better and more effective cauterization.
The Fifth Chapter.
Concerning Cerebral Hemorrhages.
If pain occurs in the ear due to cold and it has been treated with poultices and all the treatment that we mentioned in the division, and the pain does not subside, then guard the point that is called the nodule which this resembles.
Then wrap it with that after warming it around all the ears just like it wraps around them both if the pain is in both. And remove the ligature from the root of the ear a little after learning the position with ink, and the ligature should be about ten points in each ear or around it. Then treat the positions until it is cured if Allah wills.
The sixth chapter.
In the ligature of the claw.
The ligature which is treated with the ligature is only that of the type which occurs from phlegm as I mentioned in the divisions of diseases.
And avoid the ligature of the type which occurs from membranes and stretching of the nerve.
When you treated this type of ligature with poultices, compresses, and cupping and it did not benefit your treatment then the patient should be treated with three ligatures. One at the root of the ear, the second slightly below the cheekbone, and the third at the junction of the lips.
And make your ligature on the opposite side of the affected part because relaxation only occurs in the healthy side.
And the shape of the ligature is to apply it as a ligature on the side of the upper part of the ear under the temporal bone slightly, and another one on the cheekbone, and its length should be according to the length of the eyebrow.
You bring your hand down with the ligature until you burn a quarter of the skin thickness, and this is the shape of the cauterization and it is a type of cauterization which I mentioned its form earlier but it is slightly softer than that as you see. And it is necessary for the cauterizer to be a little thicker, then treat the place as mentioned earlier until it is cured if Allah wills.
The Seventh Chapter.
On Chronic Hemorrhage.
If you have treated the hemorrhage and applied what we mentioned, but your treatment has not been effective and there is no apparent cause of fever, then perform four ligatures. One ligature at the top of his head and another in the middle of the head, as we mentioned, and one in the occiput of the head, above what has been mentioned.
And the recipe for the caustic substance is as previously mentioned, and it may also be applied with a ligature to the mouth of the stomach, which will make it more effective, then treat as previously mentioned.
The Eighth Chapter.
On Amputation.
He who has a condition caused by phlegm should first be given an infusion of large doses of purgative herbs and cleansing agents for the brain.
Then he should have his entire head shaved and a poultice of mustard plaster, as described in the chapter on ulcers, be applied to the occiput repeatedly, for it is one of the remedies.
And do that to the affected area, exactly as described there, for he will be cured by doing so; otherwise, perform three ligatures on his occiput, arranged from the top of the head to the neck.
And place a thick finger's width between each ligature and the next, then treat as previously mentioned; if you wish to increase it and the patient is capable of withstanding it, perform the middle ligature.
If you wish to increase it, perform another ligature on the temples, then treat until he is cured; and the caustic substance will be resinous in accordance with what has been previously mentioned.
The Ninth Chapter.
On Apoplexy and Relaxation of the Entire Body.
He should be given an infusion of purgative herbs and what we mentioned, then have his head shaved and a ligature applied in the middle of the head, a ligature on each temple of the head, and a ligature on the occiput.
If three fingers are applied to the vertebrae of the neck, and it is necessary to relax the body further due to a strong and steady disease, then place four fingers on the vertebrae of his back. And make the poultice adhere until most of it is burned into the skin, then lift your hand and treat him as mentioned earlier until he recovers if Allah wills, and the poultice shall be ointment-like.
The Tenth Chapter.
In the case of epilepsy.
For indeed, the one who is seized with epilepsy that arises from phlegm should first cleanse his brain with large vessels and all other treatments mentioned in the division, if the illness is great and possible for taking medicine.
And as for the one who is a child and cannot tolerate medicine, then use the clarifying and purging substances for the brain several days before that, with improvement of his diet.
Then have him shaved and place one poultice in the middle of his head as mentioned in the description, and another in his occiput. And on each horn of his head, a poultice; if the patient is strong and can tolerate it, then place the poultices mentioned for the one with epilepsy and relax the body on the vertebrae of the neck and back, and the poultice shall be ointment-like as described.
If the illness is in a child, then make the poultice gentle on this shape.
The Eleventh Chapter.
In the case of melancholy.
If the cause of melancholy is putrid humors and thick phlegm, then place the poultices mentioned for one with epilepsy.
If the cause of melancholy is leaning towards darkness and the body of the patient is wet and putrid, then cleanse his brain as mentioned in the division.
Then cut off the patient's head, then make a firm cake from linen, like a circle. Then put it in the middle of his head, and the patient sitting upright, holding from each side, then take one piece from old goat suet.
Then heat it on the fire, moderately hot, as much as the finger can endure if inserted into it. Then put it in the middle of his head, in the circle, and leave it until it cools. Do that with the patient every week, along with good management, until he recovers, if God wills.
And if you wish, wet it with many small dots, not grasping the instrument with your hand but with a gentle touch; for this type of wetting cools the brain moderately.
Then put a soaked thread on him, in the suet or in chicken fat.
The Twelfth Chapter.
Regarding the water that falls into the eye.
If you notice the water that falls into the eye, indicating the symptoms mentioned in the classification, then begin to cleanse the patient's head and body of all impurities and bathe him in a bath with soap for several days.
Then pass a thread around his head and tie it in the middle of the head, then tie two threads on the temples if the water begins to flow into both eyes or from one side only if it is in one eye.
Then cut with the instrument all the veins and arteries under the skin, making sure that the threads are there in length along the temples and prevent bleeding.
If you see anything from it, cut it at the spot using any treatment possible and we will come to the wisdom of binding the arteries and cutting them and preventing bleeding.
And two threads can be tied in the occiput under the bones.
The Thirteenth Chapter.
In Chronic Cases of Weeping.
If the tears of the eye are chronic and persistent, and it is due to blood vessels and membranes which appear on the surface of the head from outside the head, and I have ascertained that this is due to a thick, gelatinous discharge reaching the canal I described at the beginning of the flow of water. A canal in the middle of the head, and two canals on the temples, and two under the occipital bones, and if necessary, I would increase the canal at each side of the eye on the margin of the eyebrow with a small instrument.
The Fourteenth Chapter.
In Chronic Cases of Nasal Discharge.
If he has been treated as mentioned in the chapter and the treatment did not succeed, then he should apply a poultice of tar for three nights and then shave his head and open up the central canal with an ointment instrument. Then open up with the vermilion instrument two canals above the eyebrows, a little beneath the hair, and be careful not to cut the artery; this is the shape of the vermilion.
The Fifteenth Chapter.
In Chronic Cases of Relaxation of the Eyelid.
If the eyelid relaxes due to disease or moisture, open up the eyelid with this crescent-shaped instrument.
And if you wish, open up above the eyebrows a little, two canals on each side, and keep them apart from the temples, and let the length of each canal be as long as the eyebrow.
And do not overdo it with the canal, but to the extent that one-third of the skin is burned, and this is the shape of the instrument.
The Sixteenth Chapter.
In Chronic Cases of Eyelid.
If it is turned upside down into the socket, then the upper part of the eye should be cut out and the rest will be like that. Either it is cauterized with fire or it is treated with a burning medicine, so if it is cauterized with fire, the patient should be told to stop shaving his eyebrows until they grow long and even.
If it is pulled out when it is growing, then bind his eyes with a bandage so that they do not move until it grows and becomes even. When it has grown and become even, place the patient's head on a stone and mark the eyelid of the eye with ink in the shape of an aspen leaf.
And the mark will begin near the eyebrows, then place a thread dyed in white of egg or in masticated mulberry under the eyelid, and preserve this image.
Then rub it gently, a little at a time, many times until the surface of the skin which is in the shape of an aspen leaf becomes all rough and distinct, and a sign of the success of your work that you will see the eyelid raised up and the hair risen above the edge of the eye.
Then raise your hand at that time and leave it for three days, then place a thread with fat on it until the scab falls off, then treat it with ointment until it clears up if God wills. If anything of the hair returns after some time and the eyelid relaxes.
Then re-treat the area as you did initially, if the hair is in the lower eyelid, remove it until it returns to its natural place and does not fall onto the eye. And if it is treated with a burning medicine, then tell the patient to stop shaving his eyebrows until they grow long and even.
Then make an image of an aspen leaf from paper, then take from the familiar soap and unground gypsum each one weighing a dirham or so, and crush them both together thoroughly with a mortar until they are well mixed. Then stretch it out on the cloth you have prepared, in the shape of a asphodel leaf, and place it on one or both eyelids. Put a moistened thread under the eye and a headrest in your stone.
And place your index finger above the medicine and press it lightly as you move it whenever the patient feels a craving for the medicine because he finds pleasure in it like fire. As long as he finds pleasure, leave the medicine and move your finger; if the pleasure subsides, remove the medicine and wash the eye with water.
And look; if you see the eyelid has risen like it rises when burned or cut, otherwise, repeat the treatment on the part where the medicine did not take effect and was not absorbed until you complete your work and the eye calms down, then put a cotton swab with fat on it until the scab forms.
Then treat it with the almond ointment or other until it heals, and it is necessary for you to be extremely careful when working so that nothing from the medicine falls into the eye, for if the eyelid relaxes after some days and hair grows in the eye.
Then repeat the treatment on that part of the eyelid which has relaxed, just as you did at first, then treat it until it heals, and this is the shape of an asphodel leaf.
And know that people's eyes may differ in size and shape, so adjust your treatment accordingly. And there is no way to go astray for one who has experience with this craft.
The Seventeenth Chapter.
About the cornea that appears in the eye socket.
If you treated the cornea as we mentioned in the sections of diseases and it did not benefit from your treatment, then you should attribute this to its nature.
The patient should place his head on a pillow and have it held in position by an attendant between your hands, not moving or striking his head.
Then you should put a moist thread in the white of an egg or on the tongue of a leech and apply it to his eyes, then cover the bandage with this shape.
It will be shaped like a falcon's tube, one end being the part with the knot and if you wish it to be open at the other end or if you wish it to be closed like a reed, but this shape is better for your work, God willing.
Then you should cut the ligament if it is open and remove the excess and clean it, or if it is not open then you should open it and extract the clot, and then place the bandage on it, which is very protective, so that you can hold onto it with your hand until you reach the bone.
And move your hand a little when reaching the knot, from the eye to the direction of the nose, so that your hand does not err or disturb the patient, and the bandage does not fall into the eye socket and damage it. If you reach the bone in the first attempt, and if not, then redo the bandage once again if necessary.
And leave it for three days, then apply a thread with fat and treat him with dried ointment until he recovers. If it is not healed after forty days, then apply the strong and severe medicine until the bone is exposed, and consider what will be mentioned later in its chapter, God willing.
And the last part of the ligament, mentioned by some of the early ones, aims at the location of the ligament, cuts it, and then puts into the same cut a thin pessary, this is its shape.
And fill it with the weight of a lead dirham, dissolved and hold your hand on the pessary firmly, tightly grasped, without the patient moving at all, lest the melted lead flows into his eye. It is necessary to put a moist thread in the white of an egg or in water on the patient's eye.
If the lead corrodes it will burn the nasal passage and free it in a wondrous way, if the nasal passage is freed as mentioned earlier from the knot and treatment; otherwise, it is necessary to use nasal piercing and direct the lead back into the nasal passage as will be mentioned in its specific place.
The Eighteenth Chapter.
In the division of the cheek.
Often a split occurs in the cheek, which is called "shirra", and especially in children's cheeks, for it often happens; if you treat this split as mentioned in the division and the treatment does not succeed, then attach a small skin-thin splint to it like this.
It will be placed in the groove of the splint, then the applicator will put it in the same split until the knot reaches the depth of the split, then treat it with cautery until it is healed, if God wills.
The Nineteenth Chapter.
In the division of the nasal passage occurring in the mouth.
If it appears in the gum, or in the uvula, or in the roots of the teeth and becomes a boil that bursts and becomes a nasal passage then treated but the treatment was unsuccessful, it is necessary to apply a splint as much as can fit into the nasal passage.
Then the applicator will put it in the nasal passage and hold your hand until the cautery reaches its upper and lower parts, and do that once or twice, then treat it after that with what is mentioned from the treatment until it is healed, if God wills.
If the material is torn and it is freed; otherwise, it is necessary to uncover the place and remove the rotten bone according to what will be mentioned in its chapter, if God wills.
The Twentieth Chapter.
On clefts and loose teeth.
If the tooth has become loose due to moisture and the clefts have been treated with medicine, but it did not heal; then put the patient's head in a vice and bind the splint which is shown after this, once you place the tube on the molar.
And the splint enters into it, guarded by a wheel, and you hold your hand a little until the patient feels the heat of the fire has reached the root of the molar; then lift your hand and repeat the splint as many times as you want, then fill the patient's mouth with saltwater.
And you hold it for an hour and then let go, because the loose molar is set right and the tooth becomes firmer, and the foul moisture dries up.
The twentieth chapter.
On pain of the molar.
If the pain of the molar is due to cold or there is an abscess, and the treatment with medicine did not heal; then the solution is on two faces: either the application of fat or the application of fire.
The application of fat is that you take cow fat, boil it in an iron pot or a cauldron, then take a string and wrap it around the end of the molar, then immerse it in the boiled fat and place it on the aching tooth with a wheel and hold it until it cools.
Then repeat it several times until the heat of the fire reaches the root of the molar, and if you wish, immerse a cloth or string in cold fat and place it on the aching tooth and put a protected iron above it until the fire reaches the base of the tooth.
And the application of fire is that you take a copper or iron tube with some roughness in it, so that the heat of the fire does not reach the patient's mouth, then bind the splint which is shown and place it on the same tooth and hold your hand until the splint cools, do this several times.
If the wound goes away either that very day or the next, it is necessary after that to fill the mouth of the patient with good fat and hold it for an hour then spit it out, and this is the shape of the poultice.
Cut with whatever side you wish and on the depth that allows, and this is the shape of the tube.
The 22nd chapter.

The Twenty-Seventh Chapter.
Of the Cold Liver.

The Twenty-Eighth Chapter.
Of the Lumps of the Liver Treated with Poultices.

And if it is in the membranes of the liver, then with the pain there will be intense sharpness and I have seen that doctors have failed to treat it, so the patient should lie down on his back then apply a poultice to the swelling.
Then the flaps are protected in fire, and it is the flap which resembles the scale, and this is its form. The nineteenth chapter.

The 30th Chapter.

The Forty-Ninth Chapter.
In the sciatic nerve.
If pain occurs in the hip and its cause is cold and dampness, and you treated the ailment as mentioned earlier and the treatment did not succeed, then it becomes necessary to loosen the blockage with a hot compress or a mustard poultice or something similar.
Then bind a poultice to the incision, either with caustic medicines or with fire. The fire-caused incision will be on many faces, one of them being to cauterize the sciatic hip itself three times in this shape.
And it will have a suitable depth, and after each incision there will be a gap the width of a finger, and the poultice will be olive-like. And you can cauterize one incision in the middle on top of the hip itself, making four incisions, or if you want, use the circular instrument mentioned earlier for removing the sciatic nerve, as one incision.
So that the circle encircles all of the sciatic hip and burns through all the skin, this is the nature of the cauterization in sciatica if the pain persists only in the hip itself and does not extend to the thigh and leg.
If it extends to the thigh and leg, then cauterize two incisions on the thigh in the place that the pain indicates is affected there, one above the sciatic notch by four fingers towards the outside slightly, and make the poultice thin and the depth of the incision only as deep as the thickness of the skin.
And if it indicates that the pain extends to about the toes, then cauterize where it has indicated to you with a poultice three or four times or more as needed, and if it indicates the pain under the knee towards the leg, then cauterize there one thin incision.
Guard yourself in all your acts so that you do not reach with it to the bone or a large artery, lest you cause the patient a bad condition or injury.
And I have seen one man after another whose bone was cut above the ankle and reached into the leg, until it pierced the foot and caused all of it to rot and corrupted the entire leg, then diarrhea and death followed; if the pain is in both legs similarly, their condition will be like this.
And some wise scholars have mentioned in the treatment of sciatica that they make a cauldron from iron, its diameter being half a finger's breadth, and at the mouth it is as thick as a date stone or slightly thinner; inside that cauldron there is another cauldron and yet another.
And it will be that between each cauldron there is a space equal to the width of an eyebrow, and the cauldrons are open on both sides and their height is about the length of an eyebrow or two; and for them a lid is made from iron well-fitted onto the cauldrons, this is its shape.
Then it is heated in the fire until it becomes red-hot, and the patient is then placed on a wooden board with the afflicted leg hanging off to the right side, and it is cauterized three times in one sitting; then it is left for three days, and it is smeared with fat and the wound is left open.
Many then treat it with an ointment until it heals, he said. This book contains this type of sciatica, we have rarely used it to cure it and its appearance is frightening, except that few find patience for it, but for those who do and are treated accordingly.
And as for the sciatica with burning medicines, it is that you make two cauldrons like a ring where mercury or iron powder is poured.
The wounds in their crevices will be about the height of two or three inches and will have a gap between them as thick as a finger. The bottom one will be open, the top one open, and some part of it will be grasped together in this shape.
Then you will place it on the curved part of the thigh and the patient lying on his healthy side, grasping your hand gently. Then pour between the two circles of hot water, which has been warmed by a little fire, and hold it for the duration of a sandy hour. The patient endures the pain and burning as if he were in a fire.
Until the pain subsides, then raise your hand with the instrument and wipe away the hot water from the thigh completely with sweet water. Then leave it for three days and apply oil on it until the burns' darkness goes away. Leave it some more time until pus comes out, as that is more beneficial.
Then treat it with ointments until it heals. If the pain spreads to the thigh or leg, make a compress of the same type that you used on the thigh, regardless. This is the quality of hot water and I have proven it in my treatise on the correction of medicines.
Take a part from the unslaked lime and a part from the unslaked gypsum, each one separate. Then grind them together and put them in a new container that has been hollowed out at the bottom with a small hole just big enough for the spatula to enter.
And pour on the lime and gypsum from sweet water until it covers them up to the finger, after having grasped them firmly with your hand. Then leave the container until the hot water descends into the hollowed-out part of the container. Then gather all that water together and pour it on another lump of gypsum and another lump of lime, again also.
And so it becomes very strong and active in many medical operations and for all other organs, because it does the action of fire exactly. And among medicines that treat the thigh are also Thapsia and Balaustium honey with ground gypsum mixed with soap.
Galenus narrated the story of a man from ancient times who treated a case of sciatica and lumbago. He greatly emphasized its importance and claimed that it does not require any other treatment, and that it cures once only.
Until he has entered the bath wrapped and emerged cured, and it is said to take some green saffron, if it is not found, to use dry modern saffron with something of fat and place it on the back where the pain is or in the leg or in the thigh.
And it is stretched and left for three hours or as long as the patient feels relief from the warmth, then enter him into the bath. If he becomes warm in his body, enter him into the basin. The pain goes away and cures by God's will, if not, repeat the poultice on him after ten days again.
And it cures if God wills, and know that no one should use these remedies except after purging the body. And Diascusrides mentioned that if goat's fleece is applied to lumbago, it brings benefit.
And the poultice is of this kind, it takes wool and dips it in old oil and places it on the deep place between the elbow and the wrist, which is closer to the wrist. Then take a goat's fleece that is dry.
Then heat it with fire until it becomes a coal, then place it on the wool and leave it until it is extinguished, then take another one and continue to do so until the sensation reaches through the shoulder to the back and the pain subsides by God's will, and this type of poultice is called the goat's fleece poultice.
The 42nd Chapter.
In the treatment of a backache.
The pain in the back may be due to many causes, either from a fall or blow or excessive fatigue and so on, and it is caused by accumulation of cold damp matter, and this poultice only falls into this category.
Whoever causes a cold substance to be poured on the patient, it is necessary after evacuating the patient's bowels and the like that he lies down on his back where the pain occurs, three rows wide on the same width as the table itself, after having learned the position by means of ink on each row five or more strokes according to what you see from the patient's ability and strength.
And it will be the stroke with a rounded point, or if you wish, three or four strokes with a rounded point, moderately spaced in this manner.
The Third Section and Tenth Part.
At the beginning of the incision.
