The Fourth Section and Forty-First Part.
In the stroke for gout and joint pains.
If the joint pains are from cold humors and settle on any part of the body, then if the pain occurs in both legs, it is usually customary among doctors to call that gout proper.
If the cold gout is not relieved by the treatment mentioned in the previous section, and the pains persist, then the stroke goes to it and that is done by making many strokes after evacuating around the joints of the legs with a rounded point moderately spaced on this shape.
If you need to puncture the man's face, do it with a pointed instrument. If the pain rises to the knees or to other joints, and this often happens, apply three or four strokes of this ointment from each side to every knee with that pointed instrument in particular.
If you need more than this stroke, apply it, but do not deepen your finger with the stroke; rather, let it be as if you are stroking the skin only. If the pain rises to the hips or to the back, use what we mentioned earlier of the stroke in its place.
If the pain is only in the hands, puncture around the wrists as if you were wrapping two folds. If the pain remains in the fingers, puncture each joint with a point and at the tip of the hand, if the pain rises after days to the elbows or armpits.
Punctuate both sides and the patient will not be deprived of good treatment and taking medication, for if he eats well and expels phlegm, he will recover with this stroke, God willing.
The 45th Chapter.
In the matter of ulcers.
If an ulcer appears in the abdomen and some of the intestines or entrails descend to the genitals, and this is at the beginning, it is necessary that the patient be ordered not to eat for a day and to use what can help to evacuate the bowel from his belly.
Then he will lie down before you on his back and you will order him to hold himself until the entrails or intestines protrude, then return them with your finger. Then, learn by drawing a line under the ulcer on the bone of the hip, as if it were half a circle with its edges extending upwards along the body.
Then protect this ointment shape.
Until it becomes white and cools the inflammation, then return the entrails or intestines to his belly. Then, have a servant place his hand on the spot so that the entrails do not protrude again; I have placed a cushion between the patient's legs and another servant has tied up his legs.
And the last on his chest grasps his hands, then the retractor falls on the mark itself and your hand with the retractor stands upright and holds it until it reaches the bone or returns it once more if it does not reach the bone at first.
And conserve your effort from exposing the intestines while you are cutting, lest they be burnt and as a result either death or great harm will occur to the patient. And know that whenever you do not reach the bone with your cut, your operation will not be successful, and the retractor of children should be gentle on their bellies and for adults on theirs.
Then treat the wound with ghee after three days until the dryness of fire goes away, then treat it with other ointments until it heals. And let the patient lie on his back for forty days until the wound is closed.
And it is necessary to make his food last throughout his treatment, so that his stomach will be easy on him, lest the intestines emerge when he urinates or defecates. Then, if he wants to get up after forty days, use a strong bandage and keep it in place for another forty days, and gradually reduce his fatigue, thirst, eating and drinking, and loud shouting.
For if you use this treatment in this way, he will recover completely, God willing. And I will mention the treatment of an incision by an incision in its chapter, God willing. As for the hernia that occurs in the entire abdomen and was initially present, if you want to prevent it from increasing, make a circular incision around it according to its size. And let what is burned from the skin be like a third of it, then treat it as we mentioned. For it will not increase, God willing. And some earlier ones have said that one should suture the hernia with a triangular retractor in this shape.
After learning to suture the wound with thread and making the two lines, one on the upper side of the wound and the other below it, and putting your hand in the middle with great care, the first finger being easier and better if God wills.
The Forty-Eighth Section.
In the wound's depth.
If an injury occurs in some organs due to a fall or blow and the pain persists for a long time, despite treatment with medicines, then it is necessary to cauterize with a burning point, each finger being according to the size, smallness, weakness, and strength of each member.
And the pain and wound is removed from it, then he is freed from the first burn, otherwise, you should repeat the burning on him because these pains have a habit of transferring from one member to another nearby, therefore, you should follow them with a burn until the patient recovers.
The Forty-Seventh Section.
In the leprosy wound.
As for those suffering from leprosy, they may benefit greatly from the cauterization, especially the type of leprosy that is caused by the yellowish phlegm and blackness.
If you wish to cauterize it, look at the leprosy; if it is initial and you have treated it as mentioned in the section, and it has not subsided nor stopped, and the patient's flesh is weak and susceptible to decay, then apply five burns on the head. The first one in the middle of the head, the second one below it towards the forehead at the end of the hairline, two on the temples and one from behind on the occipital protuberance; direct your hand with the cauterizing instrument slightly until it has a slight effect on the bone.
And it will shed off scales, making it easier to exhale the thick vapors from it and cauterize it with a burn also on the same spot as mentioned earlier; but if the leprosy has continued on the patient and has shown a clear appearance, then you should apply these burns that we mentioned on the head. Placement on the nose, two placements on the cheekbones, two placements on the neck vertebrae, six on the back vertebrae, one large placement at the coccyx when the anus is empty and another above it in the same position, two on each thigh, one on each. Two on the kneecaps, one on each knee, two on the shoulders, two on the elbows, two on the chest straps, and one on every joint of his hands and feet.
And take care not to injure the nerve at the back of the heels, lest you cause them harm. And know that every application is more effective and safer the more you apply it.
And know that the patient does not feel pain from the application as the healthy person does because his body is numb, and it is necessary to have needle thicknesses of large and small according to the parts and joints as mentioned earlier.
Then treat the application with refined honey and all other treatment until it heals, if God wills.
The 48th chapter.
When a member of the limbs becomes numb and has been treated with medicines, poultices, and bandages but did not heal, then treat that same numb member with applications according to its bone's thickness or smallness.
Then treat it with ointment until it heals, and sometimes for some numbness that appears on the hand and foot in the back vertebrae at the exit of the nerve that moves that member, then the numbness departs.
And he should not proceed with that unless he is knowledgeable about dissecting the limbs and exits of the nerves that move the body.
The Forty-Ninth Chapter.
About Gout.
If the gout persists and no remedy from the remedies of medicine is effective, then make an incision in it a little deep to the thickness of the skin until the whitish part goes away and its color changes.
Then treat it with a fine paste of broad beans, mixed with rosewater, the sap of the castor oil plant, or the blood of the finch, from each one a portion, and mix all together, and apply it to a cloth, and bind it to the place until it heals.
The Fiftieth Chapter.
About Cancer.
If the cancer is newly formed and you want to stop it, then encircle it with a circular file as it rotates. And some wise men have said that one should make an incision in its center, but I do not see this, because I expect it to ulcerate and I have seen this happen on many occasions.
The correct thing is to incise around it in a circle as we said, or with multiple cuts.
The Fifty-First Chapter.
About Dropsy.
If dropsy occurs in someone and it delays in its development either due to the active humour that affects it or due to the age of the patient if he is an old man with little blood or due to time, and you want to hasten the development of the dropsy, then make many small cuts around it, pouring.
Then leave it, because it hastens in its development. If you want to remove it with a file, take care of the file that has this shape.
And lower it into the middle of the dropsy until it penetrates the skin and be like what is below, so that it may be easy to remove the pus, then treat it as needed until it heals.
The Second Fifty Chapter.
In the Matter of Food.
The ulcer is nothing but decay that eats away at the organ as fire consumes dry wood. If you see an ulcer in a place where it may catch fire, use many small and large poultices as needed for that location where there is the ulcer.
Then surround it from all sides until the decay is completely removed and nothing remains of it whatsoever. Then leave it for three days and apply the sulfur powder mixed with oil to the affected areas until all the crust and all the decay are gone.
Then treat it with soothing ointments for the flesh. If after three days you see that the flesh is growing new and healthy tissue, free from decay, otherwise reapply the treatment to what remains of the affected areas, and the ulcer can be treated with a harsh medicine.
For it is more effective with fire, and I have mentioned its treatment with harsh medicine in the previous chapter; take it from there whenever you need to.
The Third Fifty Chapter.
In the Matter of the Reversed and Unreversed Pliers.
This affliction often occurs in the soles of the feet and is something harsh that troubles the man, and the treatment for it is on two counts: either with fire or with harsh water.
As for the treatment with fire, it is that you make a small iron tool resembling an eagle's beak, which surrounds the pincer from all sides and has a thin rim. Then you place the tool on top of the pincer and turn your hand around the pincer until the tool reaches the depth of the pincer.
And leave it for three days until it forms a scab, then wrap it in powdered bread soaked in salt and leave the dressing on overnight. When morning comes, it will have separated from its roots; then treat the wound with soothing ointment for the flesh until it heals, if the pincer is not reversed.
Many times an abscess occurs on the surface of the body, especially in the hands and feet. Therefore, it is necessary to take a tube from copper or iron or eagle's feathers and place it on the abscess or boil, then pour into the tube a small amount of hot water.
You grasp your hand and while rotating it slightly, you make the tube's rim touch the edge of the abscess. Then the hot water finds its way into the abscess's root. The patient endures the hot water for a moment.
Then leave it alone, as the abscess bursts open at its roots. Do this with each one separately until you have treated all of them in the body. Then treat the areas after the abscesses have burst open and the flesh has been cleansed with ointments.
The Fourth Chapter Fifty.
In cases of Fistula.
If a fistula occurs due to cold on the nerve or quartan fever or any other cause, it is necessary to apply four or five compresses on the back between each compress and one in the chest. And on his abdomen, a compress with oilcloth compression, so that the fistula subsides and hastens the maturation of the cold disease.
The Fifth Chapter Fifty.
In cases of Pus in the Body.
It may break out on the body as foul boils caused by cold, thick, and rotten matter. Therefore, when they first appear, you should apply a soft compress to each boil with a stick that has been burned at one end or with the long root of the safflower plant or with an oilcloth compression.
And you should apply the poultice to the boils at their first appearance in this way, so that it does not increase and the pus-producing discharge is dissipated from it, and the patient becomes free of it, except that this should happen after the patient has been purged with phlegm.
The 50th chapter.
In the event of bleeding that occurs when cutting a vein.
Blood from a severed artery often flows copiously when an external wound is inflicted or when a tumor or limb is divided, and it becomes difficult to cut.
So, if that happens to someone, hasten with your hand to the mouth of the artery and place your thumb on it tightly until the blood is stopped under your thumb and nothing comes out from it. Then, take a small or large olive pit, whichever you have available, and hold it over the fire until it becomes very hot.
Then take one, either small or large, according to the wound and the location where the artery was cut, and place it on the same vein after removing your thumb with ease and hold the olive pit until the bleeding stops.
If the bleeding starts again when you lift your thumb from the mouth of the artery and stop applying the olive pit, take another olive pit with ease from the ones in the fire that are prepared and continue to do this one after another until the bleeding stops.
And be careful not to burn the surrounding tissue, as this may cause another wound on the patient. And know that if an artery bleeds, it cannot be cut, especially if the artery is large, except through one of four openings, either by ligating as we said, or by cauterizing if it has not been severed. And if it is cauterized, its ends will shrink and the bleeding will stop. Either wrap it tightly with threads or apply medications that can cut off the bleeding and bind it securely with ligatures.
And as for someone who attempts to cut it with a ligature or bind it tightly with a compress or apply burning substances and so on, then that will not stop the bleeding at all except in rare cases; if anyone has done this without a doctor's attention or remedy, let him first place his thumb on the mouth of the wound itself as we described.
You compress the wound extremely until the blood congeals and drips from above the wound onto the artery and finger, and it does not come away from him with cold water always, until the blood freezes and thickens and stops. In that moment you look to see what it needs in terms of poultice or medicine.
The Second Chapter.
In the incision, the excision, the lance wound and similar injuries.
He said: What we mentioned in the first book regarding every disease that requires cauterization and burning medicine, its causes, reasons and instruments, and illustrations of surgical procedures, I have divided into chapters from the beginning to the end.
And I follow in this chapter that same path so as not to make it difficult for the student what is required of him.
Before I begin with that, oh my sons, you should know that this chapter contains some of the things that are above what is in the first book on cauterization.
And for that reason, it is necessary to warn against it strongly because the work in this chapter is great and often falls into wasting blood which is the source of life when opening a vein or incision on a tumor or abscess or surgical treatment or extracting a splinter or cutting open a stone and similar things that accompany all these dangers and fears, and result in most of them in death.
And I warn you against falling into what is uncertain, for indeed there are types of people in this craft who are afflicted with various diseases, and some of them become weary of their illness and succumb to death.
Due to the severity of their illness and the length of their suffering, and because the disease has taken a turn for the worse, which indicates death, and some of them spend their wealth on you and pay your fees in the hope of regaining their health, and their illness becomes a struggle; therefore, it is not right for you to abandon those who are in this state.
Let your caution be greater than your desire and zeal, and do not proceed with anything from that unless you are certain of the outcome that will bring glory to you. And use in all treatment of your patients the principle of knowledge and warning about what will lead to salvation.
For you have in that a means to acquire praise, glory, mention, and thanks. May God guide you, my sons, to righteousness and prevent you from error and success; for that is in His Hand, there is no god but He.
And I have organized this chapter into sections, as mentioned earlier in the section on wounds, from head to toe, so that you may quickly find what you are looking for, if God wills.
The First Chapter.
In the Treatment of Water that Assembles on the Heads of Children.
This disease is often presented to children at birth if the mother presses the child's head without care, and it may also be caused by a hidden cause that is not known.
And I have not seen this condition in anyone except children, and all that I have seen of them die from it. Therefore, I saw fit to leave the treatment of it alone, and I have seen a child whose head was filled with water, and the head grows larger every day. Until the child cannot sit up by himself because of the size of his head, and the moisture increases until he dies.
And this moisture is either gathered between the skin and the bone or beneath the bone on the peritoneum. If the moisture is between the skin and the bone, and the swelling is small, then it is necessary to make a single incision in the middle of the head, about two hands' breadth long, until the moisture is drained; this is the picture of the trephine.
If the moisture increases and the swelling becomes greater, then make two crossing incisions like this:
And if the moisture is under the bone and its sign is that you see the stitches of the head opened from all directions and the water sinks when you press it with your hand to the inside, it does not matter; therefore, you should cut in the middle of the head three incisions in this shape.
And after the incision, all the moisture will come out, then you should close the incisions with sutures and bandages, then wash it from above with vinegar and oil until the fifth day, then loosen the bandage and treat the wound with poultices and ointments, and do not leave the head bound moderately, and feed the patient with all dry food little moisture.
Until the member is strong and healed, another method of incision is to look where the bone of the tumor appears and the gathering of water, because it may be in the back of the head more or in the front or in the right or in the left.
So aim at the incision where the tumor appears and the gathering of water, and make an incision as much as you can, and be careful not to cut a vein so that bleeding occurs and the patient dies from that bleeding with the moisture expelled.
The second chapter.
Cutting the two veins behind the known ears.
When someone experiences a sudden attack to the eyes or chest and no relief is obtained through medicine, then inform that the treatment in this case is cutting these two veins.
It is necessary if you want to cut them that you should shave the patient's head with a razor, then roughen the place with a coarse cloth so that the veins appear, then bind the patient's neck with his own cloth, and look where the pulsation of sweat and their two hidden places are located behind the ears, except in some people.
Then learn their course with ink, then cut them with a sharp scalpel cuts up to the bone and it will be that way around the head; if you wish, you can enter the scalpel from under the vein and push it upwards along the cut and the length of the cut will be about two folded fingers.
If the artery is severed, blood will exit with a pulsating flow and flow forward, stopping at the anterior and posterior. If the vein does not appear to be palpable, it is necessary to measure from the ear by three fingerbreadths then learn with ink and cut to the bone, which should.
Blood will flow seven or eight fingerbreadths downstream and perhaps a little more or less, all of which is according to the strength of the sufferer and the fullness of his veins. Then look at the wound; if anything remains on the bone from theomentum, cut it off.
So that a hot abscess does not form, then bind the wound with a thread from a torn cloth and treat it with ointments until it is cured.
The third chapter.
The two arteries in the armpits.
If a person has chronic sciatica or sudden attacks of sharp pains in the muscles of the armpits, or severe and prolonged headache and the like, and was treated with various medical remedies but did not benefit from that, then we have tried to ligate the arteries at the armpits or cauterize them as we described.
And the method of ligation is to shave the sufferer's hair in the armpits and direct the artery that appears on the surface of the armpit, for it will become evident to you from its pulse, except in some individuals.
Or if the cold is intense, and it is not evident to you, then have the sufferer tighten their shoulder with the help of a cloth, and then search for the place with a piece of cloth or wet the place with warm water until the artery becomes clearly visible. Then take the forceps that has this shape. Then take the forceps and peel away the skin gently until you reach the artery, then insert a ligature into it and pull it up until you can bring it out of the skin and free it from any adhesions underneath in all directions. If the artery is thin, tie it off with the edge of the ligature. Then a portion is cut off from it as much as its sides are apart and it constricts without causing bleeding, for if it does not get cut or torn, the blood will not flow at all. Then drain out six or three qata' of blood.
If the artery is large, it is necessary to suture it in two places with a strong double thread, either of silk or flax, so that decay does not occur before the wound heals and bleeding occurs.
Then cut off as much as is between the ligatures, do this at that time or later, and if you wish to shape it so that it adheres to the bone with a chisel-like instrument until its edges are trimmed, thus making this operation identical or even better as we said.
Unless the patient is feverish or in a bad mood, for the ligature ensures the elimination of moisture and makes it stronger for the benefit. Then after closing the arteries, fill the place with absorbent cotton and put on it the compressed linen, and after that treat with herbal medicines that promote flesh growth and with poultice until he is cured, if Allah wills.
If bleeding occurs from the artery during your operation, hasten to cut it off either with a ligature or by filling the place with cotton and tightening your hand until the blood stops. If nothing of that is available, press your finger until the blood coagulates.
And fill the place with cold water until the pain subsides and tightens it as needed. And what is lighter and easier than closing the artery is to shape the skin with this chisel-like instrument after the two places have been made ready with a ligature.
And bring it down firmly until it reaches the bone and the skin is cut off in two places so that what is between its edges may be separated, for it will not adhere to this ligature at all, and this is the appearance of the chisel.
The edges of the two knives are similar to small points, except that they are much less sharp because if they were as sharp as the knife, it would freeze faster and the flesh would not be cut quickly. If there is some thickness in them, they will hold up well to the heat.
I cut the flesh quickly, and this work is better than all works, lighter and easier. And let there be between the two knives a thickness equal to the tip of the finger.
The Fourth Section.
Treatment for constant and continuous bleeding from the eyes.
If the tears are constant and the bleeding comes from the veins on the back of the head outside, and nothing is benefiting in treating with medicine or remedy, and I have seen the face of the patient has turned red. And he feels in his forehead a throbbing like the throbbing of ants, and his eyes are drooping, wet, and have shriveled up their lashes and grown together from the intensity of the tears. And those who treat him resort to this practice and call it the treatment with the sword, which is that you order the patient to shave off the hair on his forehead.
Then, on the forehead, you make three parallel incisions along the length of the forehead. The length of each incision is about two fingerbreadths long, in line with the length of the nose in the middle of the forehead, the second one a little away from the movement of the muscle that is in the cheek, and the third one on the other side.
And you take care to avoid cutting the arteries that are on both sides, and keep your hand away from joining the jawbones. After each incision, there should be a distance of three folded fingers, and have with you many sponges or cloths ready to absorb the blood as it flows.
Then the surgeon inserts the sharp instrument into both sides, this is its shape. From the incision which follows the cheek to the middle incision and stripping away all the skin between the two incisions along with the peritoneum on the bone, then do the same from the middle incision to the third incision, and this probe will come out. And another instrument is inserted into the first incision, called a sharp scissor-like tool from one side and a blunt one from the other side, and this is its form:.
And its sharp side is directed upwards towards the attached flesh and its blunt side towards the bone, and it is pushed until it reaches the middle incision and cuts all the blood vessels that descend from the head to the eyes without reaching the outer skin.
Then that is done in the middle incision to the other incision, and after a moderate amount of blood has flowed, the places where the blood vessels were cut are squeezed out and then in each incision a wick made of cotton or linen dipped in wine, vinegar, or oil is placed.
So that a hot abscess does not form, and on the third day the bandage is removed and the incision is washed with plenty of cold water then it is treated with cerate made from rose oil and all that surgeons treat with until it heals if God wills.
The Fifth Chapter.
In the Treatment of Tears and Discharges to the Eyes from within the Head.
When it happens to someone that there are many sharp and continuous discharges, and you see the eyes from which they flow to be small and puffy, and their sight weakens and the eyelids become inflamed and the lashes fall out. And there is sharp and severe pain in the head, accompanied by a persistent cough; from this symptom you understand that those materials and discharges come from many deep and extensive vessels; and the best treatment for it is this treatment, which is to order the patient to blow their nose then make a single incision in the middle of the forehead.
And there is sharp and severe pain in the head, accompanied by a persistent cough; from this symptom you understand that those materials and discharges come from many deep and extensive vessels; and the best treatment for it is this treatment, which is to order the patient to blow their nose then make a single incision in the middle of the forehead. I lift it slightly with the exposure and begin to cut from the left cheekbone to the right cheekbone, making the incision up to the bone. I keep my hand away from the movable muscles of the cheek when chewing, until the bone is exposed and all the blood has been removed with a sponge.
I separate the lips of the wound with a piece of cotton or a linen thread, then pull it from above with a ligature and moisten the ligature with wine and oil so that no inflammation occurs. When I have finished and seen that the inflammation has subsided, it is necessary to scrape away the bone until new flesh begins to grow.
Then I treat it with the dried preparation that promotes flesh growth, such as taking two parts from fine emmer and four parts from sycamore, mixing them together to make a poultice, and using it for promoting flesh growth in wounds like this.
The Sixth Chapter.
Treatment of What Falls into the Ear.
All that falls into the ear is one of four types: either a mineral stone or semi-stone, such as iron and glass; or a plant seed, like mustard and dates; or something liquid, like water and vinegar.
Or a living thing. If something like a stone or a fragment of a stone falls into the ear and does not increase in size inside the ear, then receive sunlight on the ear. If you see only the stone, put some purple pitch or ceruse within it, then try to remove it by moving the head or using a catheter. Seal the nostrils when the patient has a fit of sneezing after putting a bandage around the ear made of linen or wool and stretching it upwards. Many times this treatment causes it to come out, but if not, try to remove it with the soft sponge that is its likeness.
If it emerges by the wound and not, then try to remove it with a gentle and slight bending forceps. If it does not come out with that, and not, then make a tube from copper and put the end of the tube into the ear canal.
Close the area around the tube with a tightly packed plug of grease so that there is no path for the wind except through the tube. Then pull it out with your breath, pulling strongly and repeatedly, for it often comes out like this. If it does not come out as we described, and not, then take some soap from the Nabataeans or refined soap which birds are taken with something small, and put it in the end of the tube.
After wrapping it tightly with a firm thread, then put it into the ear canal gently after the ear has dried from moisture. If it does not come out as we described, then proceed to the incision before swelling or congestion occurs.
The incision recipe is that the patient should be seated in a comfortable position or first, and then blood will flow out according to their strength. Then have the patient sit facing you, turn their ear upwards, and make a small incision in the origin of the ear at the lowest part of it.
And the incision will be crescent-shaped until it reaches the earring, then remove it with what instruments you can, and then sew up the incision as quickly as possible and treat it until it heals.
And if the thing that falls into the ear is one of the grains that grows and swells, try to remove it as we described. If you are not able to get it out, then take a thin and gentle forceps in this shape.
And try to cut that kind of grain that has fallen into the ear with this forceps, but only do so if you are certain that that grain has become fixed in the ear canal until it becomes small pieces, then remove them with a blind forceps or gentle extraction or by scraping.
As we mentioned, it is made easy to remove it. As for the water that enters the ear, it is necessary for the physician to use a syringe with kohl first, and then fill his ear with something of cotton wool while lying on that ear where there is water; if he comes out by doing so.
Or it takes many small stones from the length of the fingers, smooth ones, and warms them slightly with fire; then the physician takes one from there and inserts it into a hole in his ear, steps on one foot from that direction, and strikes another stone against the one in the ear.
He does not stop doing that with one stone after another until all the water comes out, and sometimes the water comes out by taking a piece of ice or a feather, and inserting one end into the ear and burning the other end with fire until most of it is burned, then using another feather.
He does that several times until all the water comes out or draws it with a tube as mentioned earlier, and as for removing the animal that is inside, look; if it is small like lice and the like, treat it as mentioned in the division.
If its body is large, it will be perceived by the sense; try to remove it with a pumice stone and tweezers, and make it easier than all that settles in the ear. And as for removing the worms produced in the ear if you treated them as mentioned in the division in the chapter on worms, but your treatment did not succeed.
So look at the ear in the sun; if something of the worms appears to you, remove it with a pumice stone or fine tweezers. If nothing appears to you from it, take this tube and make an image of it.
The lower part is narrow and the upper part is wide, and insert the thin end into the ear as far as the physician can manage it then grasp it firmly do that several times until all the worms come out; if they do not come out for you, seal around the tube with wax as I mentioned to you in the stones.
If it does not come out as mentioned, then use the quturats which we have mentioned and the early ones used in killing worms; you will find that in the treatise on quturats. Mix your potions and medicines into the ear with this instrument; and this is its shape:.
As you see, it is made from brass or a narrow piece of copper; there is a small hole at the bottom and a larger one at the top. If you wish, make the cannon inside the tube from firmly attached copper; if not, take a thread, wrap it tightly around the end.
Then pour the fat, juice, or whatever medicine you want into the tube which is in the ear. Then insert the thread with a cotton thread from above and press it gently with your finger until the fat flows into the auditory canal and can be felt.
With the ailing person inside, and what you poured into the ear having been warmed slightly in fire. And beware that whatever is trickling there is not extremely cold or hot, for the ear cannot tolerate that.
The Seventh Chapter.
In the Treatment of the Obstruction in the Ear.
Some children may come out of their mothers' wombs and ears unperforated.
And also, some people may have an obstruction in the ear canal due to a wound or flesh that has grown there, and this obstruction can be deep within the ear canal and not visible to the eye.
And also, some people may have an obstruction that protrudes slightly outside the canal and is visible to the eye. As for what protrudes deep within the ear and is not visible to the eye, it is usually difficult to cure. But as for what protrudes and can be seen, it is necessary to place the patient's ear in the sun. And look at it carefully; if you see the obstruction clearly, then open it with a thin forceps and this is its shape:.
The edges of the wound will have some slight exposure, some being limited and the rest being smoother on both sides so that it does not harm the ear. If the scab has formed over the flesh in the ear canal, hold it with a fine forceps and cut it off with great gentleness until all the flesh is removed.
If the scab is in the depth of the ear, take a thin and flat mica, smooth it out, heat it slightly in the fire, then insert it into the ear canal. If you feel the scab with what the patient experiences as heaviness of hearing, remove it gently.
And take care not to injure the ear canal. Then place a wick in the ear according to the size of the hole, moistening it with the Egyptian ointment. Do this for several days until you are certain that the wound is healed or take a wick and dip it in water and sprinkle powdered gum on it.
And use it. If you see the ear has become inflamed and warm, it is necessary to remove the wick and replace it with another one that has been moistened in rose fat until the inflammation subsides, then treat it until it heals.
If bleeding occurs, soak a sponge or cloth in cold water and place it on the ear. Use all the treatment that stops this type of bleeding as mentioned in the chapter on cauterization.
The Eighth Chapter.
In the treatment of ulcers which occur in the eyelids.
These ulcers that occur in the eyelids can be wet and dry. It is necessary to grasp them with a forceps or fine forceps and cut them off with a scalpel from their roots, then apply powdered gum to the area.
If bleeding occurs from it, stop it with a gentle bean-shaped pessary and bind it tightly after the cutting and often it will close if something remains of its roots. And if bound with fire, that root will be burnt up and not remain.
The Ninth Chapter.
Treatment of Prolonged Chill in the Eye Joints.
Often something resembling a chill appears in the eye joints in its severity and stubbornness.
And thus it is called a chill, being a gathering of thick moisture in the upper eyelid and lower eyelid. The treatment is to look into it; if the chill appears prominent on the surface of the eyelid, it can be divided by an incision made from above.
Then remove it from all sides gently until it is freed, then tie it up with a ligature and cut it off. If you are unable to cut it off except after the eyelid has been severed by the cutting, do not harm the patient thereby; if the incision is large, sew it up and treat it until it heals.
And if it is small, do not worry about it; the poultice will heal it and cover it. If the chill is leaning towards the inside of the eyelid towards the inner surface, turn the eyelid over and tie the chill with a ligature without needing an incision, and remove it from all sides.
And if the eyelid is severed by the cutting, it will not harm that; then wash the eye after cutting off the chill with saltwater and treat the site with what heals until the patient recovers.
The Tenth Chapter.
Treatment of Stye Which Appears in the Eyelid of the Eye.
The stye is a pustule that forms in the layers of the upper eyelid and more commonly appears on children, who are afflicted by it and suffer from night blindness, unable to gaze at the light of the sun. In order for tears to rush to them.
Therefore, they are always leaning on their faces and sleeping with them, and their eyelids become moist beneath the eyebrows due to the stench of the stye, which becomes apparent to the eye. When you press the spot with your fingers, you will feel the stye between them; and the treatment is for the patient to place his head in a stone.
Then take a piece of cotton cloth and prepare it. Make a tail from it and make a circle with it, as big as the hernia is from all sides. Then place it on it and compress it with your fingers from all sides to gather the hernia in the middle of the circle.
Then cut in the middle of that moisture with a blunt instrument, cutting it straight across and not making the cut larger than the one that is in the cicatrix. As for its depth, you should cut through all the skin until you reach the hernia.
In most cases, the hernia will protrude from the cut in the form of a white fatty piece. You then draw it out with a cloth that you have wrapped around your fingers and bring it outside while turning your hand to the right and left until it is reduced. And beware not to increase the cut lest the blunt instrument touches the eye and injures it.
If the hernia does not appear to you at first in the cut, then you should increase it slightly with care until the hernia appears. Then draw it out as we said and immerse a cloth in vinegar and water, place it on the place and bind it tightly. Some people crush salt.
And place it in the depth of the cut so that what remains of that moisture dissolves, then take care of it until it heals. If an ulcer forms in the place, treat it with gentle poultices until it heals.
The eleventh chapter.
In kinds of eye inflammation.
If a growth appears in the eyelid, extra lashes growing outside of their natural course beneath the natural lashes and falling off, then it harms the eye and causes various kinds of diseases such as continuous tearing, relaxation of the eyelids, whitening, thickening until that becomes a reason for the destruction of the eye.
And eye inflammation is in four ways, either by fire or by the sharp medicine as previously mentioned in the chapter on medicine. Or it can be caused by cutting and sewing or with papyrus as I remember.
You should place the head of the eyelid on your stone then turn the eye's lid with your left hand. If it does not flip over, then insert a needle into it from below the eyelid and push the needle through the thread from above, having that be near the same location as the hair itself, and pull the thread up onto the eyelid.
You should turn it over with the forceps then cut in the inner corner of the eyelid, avoiding the excess hair, using a curved needle from the larger to the smaller conjunctival sac. Then you should tie the thread and place a small cotton or linen strip under the eyelid, and learn on the eyelid with the styptic.
Like the shape of a sycamore leaf, but it is necessary for the shape to be according to what you want in terms of elevating the eyelid because people may differ in that, so some may need you to cut from the eyelid as much as the eyelid has relaxed.
And some may need less of all that according to the relaxation of the eyelid, then you should cut with the forceps on both lines you learned and start from the larger conjunctival sac to the smaller one, and the single incision will be near natural hair, like the thickness of a reed.
Then you should insert the suture into one of the corners of the skin, then remove it all and gather by sewing the eyelids together with a fine wool thread and needle, wipe away the blood, and secure what remains of the threads on the eyebrows with some stuck-on things if.
You may do that or not, as you please, then the suture and threads will remain for about three or four days, then treat it, and if you wish, leave the wound without suturing and treat it with what dries and contracts, because the eyelid rises when the wound is closed and the suture is better.
This is a face of the flesh incision mentioned by the earliest ones, except that it has an obligation on the patient and is one of good deeds without danger in it. And another face in the flesh incision also, namely to learn from the eyelid a shape like the shape of the tamarisk leaf as we described. Then the eyelid is raised with three hooks that are scattered or grouped in this form:.
Then what remains of the eyelid is cut off with a small scissors in this manner, cuts being made moderately:.
If you cannot hold the hooks and it is not suitable for you, take a needle with thread, insert it into the center of the shape, insert another thread nearby the larger curve, and another thread nearby the smaller curve, and gather the threads between your fingers moderately, then lift it up gently.
And lift up the skin that has been incised on it entirely as we described, then gather the edges of the wound with stitches and heal it until it is cured. If an inflammation or abscess appears at your cutting or incising, treat that inflammation with poultices and similar soothing remedies.
And if the lower eyelid also becomes disfigured, it is necessary to use what we have mentioned of incisions, stitches, and cauterization with medicine, or cauterization or medicine, more and more carefully and lightly on the patient, taking into account what has been done in this case.
Cauterization with papyrus is done in this manner: that you turn the eyelid and make a cut inside as we have described, then make two or three small incisions along the length of the eyelid and narrower than a hairbreadth.
And then the edges of both are cut off from both sides, where the threads hold on, and then they are brought together gently onto what remains of the eyelid, and the incisions are tightened firmly from both sides, and it is left for some days; for the tightened skin dies, becomes gangrenous, and putrid.
Until it falls from its place, then hasten to extract it with a pincer and treat it until it is healed. If the swelling subsides, the eyelid rises and the lashes of the eye do not protrude, this shape and size are made for the tongs in length and width exactly:.
The Twelfth Chapter.
In raising the grown-out hair from the eye with a needle.
If it is one or two hairs, the work in that is to take a thin needle and insert into it a thread of fine silk, smooth and then gather its ends together and tie them with a very delicate knot, and let the length of the thread be about an inch.
Then you will wrap around the threads another thread, a thin one, and tie its ends if you wish. Then the operator will place his head near your stone, as close to the sun as possible, so that he may see what he is doing, for it is a precise work. Then the needle enters into the bundle in the root of the excess hair.
And it will thread it through the eyelid with a needle until it comes out above the natural hair, then it will pull the thread up to above the bundle and enter into that bundle, whether one or two or three hairs.
Then you will pull your hand with it until the hair comes out with the bundle in the eyelid along with the natural hair. If you pulled the bundle and the hair did not come out with it, you will pull the bundle down with the thread that you wrapped around it until the bundle comes out of the upper hole.
Then you will put the hair back in its place and pull it until it comes out with the bundle, doing that until it rises to the upper hole and is visible to the eye. Then loosen the bundle and thread, and bring them out, and then compress the eye and leave it compressed for two or three days until the hair stays in its place and flesh grows over it.
If the hair is short, then either you add to it a long hair from natural hair and it rises with it or leave it until it lengthens after some time when it rises.
The Thirteenth Chapter.
In the treatment of the pustule which occurs in the upper eyelid of the eye.
The one exposed to this pustule is called Arnbiya and this pustule will be either natural or acquired, and the acquired one will be from an injury or a blow or a scratch or something like that.
The method of treatment is to cut that inflammation and separate its edges and insert a thread of cotton between them and tie it until it heals, and it should not be treated with things that dry and constrict.
If you do that, the pustule will return worse than it was, so use things that loosen like soap and water mixed with gum arabic and a little of the Diakhilum ointment, and apply it to the affected area.
The key to its treatment is to use every means possible so that it does not adhere to the original condition, and this method we mentioned is only some repair of the pustule, not that the place will return as it was at first.
The Fourteenth Chapter.
In the treatment of the pustule which occurs in the lower eyelid.
This pustule which is in the lower one is the one that is called Shtra and it will be either natural or acquired, and the acquired one will be from an injury or a blow or a scratch or something like that.
The method of treatment is to take a thread and tie it around the pustule, then insert an awl on either side of the pustule and push it through until the thread appears at both ends, then raise the pustule above with the awl and cut it off with a broad thumb.
If the shape of the eyelid returns to what is proper, but otherwise; take a reed and place it on the position of the incision and turn it with the eyelid and cut two flaps in the inner side of the eyelid, and the edges of the flaps will be at the angles of the cuts until they meet and form an angle. Until it meets, it will become like this shape.
And it is the Greek letter lambda, then remove that flesh as much as the sharp side of it is lower than what is next to the eyelid, then gather the separated parts with two stitches and sew it with a wool thread, then treat it with the medicines we mentioned earlier until it heals.
And if the wound is exposed from an incision or stitching or cutting, it is necessary to cut a small incision without hair on the eyelid also as mentioned earlier, then separate the lips with ointment as described.
And the sum of the statement in treating the wound whether from above or below is to work according to what appears to you about the shape of the wound, for it may be many in its appearance, and the skilled craftsman arranges the technique in any way possible.
Until the shape returns to its natural state or approaches it, and the same disease guides you about what is suitable for it in most cases.
The fifteenth chapter.
In the adhesion of the eyelid to the palpebra or to the conjunctiva.
This adhesion may expose many people to the eyelid above being attached to the white of the eye, preventing it from moving easily and impeding its natural functions, so it is necessary for you to insert a reed under the eyelid.
And lift it up or straighten it with a thread then cut the adhesion with a fine knife not being too harsh to cut off the knife so as not to disturb the operator and let the knife fall gently on the eye, and your cutting will be like peeling off that adhesion.
Until the eyelid returns to its natural state and all adhesion is resolved, then wash the eye with saltwater or instill in it a solution of black myrrh dissolved in water. Then separate the eyelid from the eye with a piece of cotton thread.
She puts a soaked wool cloth moistened with egg white over the eye, and after the third day she uses medicated threads until it heals.
The Sixteenth Chapter.
In cutting the fingernail and removing the nail bed.
The nail is either brittle and resembles a thin, hard scale, or it is non-brittle and resembles a white, solidified moisture, if touched with iron or taken by force with pincers, it will break.
And if a pincer does not stick, both types begin from the larger nail bed and gradually grow until they cover the gaze and prevent light and eye movement, and the method of cutting it is for the operator to place his head on a block.
Then he opens his eyes and raises the eyelid with your hand, then you pick up the nail with a slightly curved pincer, stretch it upwards, then take a needle, enter a hair from horse or cow hair and strong thread into it, bend the tip of the needle slightly and insert it in the middle of the nail.
And push it with the needle, tie the nail with the thread, stretch it upwards and strip off the side of the nail next to the pupil as if you were spreading it with a hair to its end, then cut the rest at the root of the nail bed with a thin pair of scissors or a small trimming tool and leave the natural nail bed.
So that the cut nail does not expose a constant flow of tears, and the nail can be stretched with a pincer alone or with thread as we said, then strip off the smooth edge on one side like this:
Be cautious not to touch the operator with the gauze, for if so, a festering would occur in it and the pupils would be narrowed, then after the cutting, something like powdered salt or crushed zanzibar stone would be found in the eye and it is left until the next day then treated as necessary so that it heals.
If the ulcer is not inflamed and you are unable to insert a needle or attach a catheter into it, this type of ulcer is often treated with medicines so that it heals as I described in the classification. And if you want to cut it, open the patient's eye.
Take a fine, soft, and weak-edged scalpel according to this shape:. Gently remove the scab from above, using a soft and gentle touch. If you see it cracking and falling apart, apply to the eye some crushed zanzibar stone or red ochre powder or powdered salt and close the eye until the next day.
Then redo the work until all of them are gone, except if there is a hot swelling in the eye; leave it and treat the swelling until it heals, then redo the work with the scab until it heals, and as for the meat that remains.
If the remnant is causing intense pain to the eye, tie off that remnant with a catheter and cut some of it off, but do not concentrate on the cutting so as not to cause bleeding then apply red ochre or zanzibar stone powder to the area until it heals.
The Seventeenth Section.
In cutting the redness and what grows from excess flesh in the eye.
In some people's eyes, excess flesh may grow red and accumulate to cover the surface of the eye or approach it or overflow onto the eyelids, and sometimes the eyelids may turn outward and resemble a pomegranate.
The operation involves the patient placing their head on a stone, then opening their eyes and tearing off all that red flesh with suitable tweezers.
Or he should grasp it with a pumice stone or gauze, then cut the flesh little by little until all of it is cut off and take care not to hurt his eye while working, and your cutting tool will be either the one we described for cutting toenails or a small scissors. As is done with the folds of skin according to what appears in this chapter.
Then, if your cutting is complete and all the redness has gone, wash the eye with crushed salt or sprinkle red camphor and similar medicines into it, and apply a thread of egg white on top from outside to prevent inflammation.
If there remains any redness and the bleeding is severe, causing inflammation to occur, leave the eye alone and treat it with what calms the inflammation, then return to it after it has healed and perform the operation again on the excess flesh that appears in the eye of this kind.
Unless you should avoid treating any weak eye through cauterization or exposure to the operation with iron, and do not put your hand into anything of this kind until you see that that organ is capable of undergoing that operation.
The Eighteenth Chapter.
On Removing the Folds from the Eye.
The folds are red veins that form on the eye, preventing sight and causing the eye to become weak with time. It is necessary for you first to examine whether the eye containing the folds is strong and not affected by any other disease except for the folds.
So then the operation is to order the patient to place their head on a stone, then tie those veins with one or two tweezers as per your skill, and the tweezers will be gentle in their curvature.
There are two double sutures in one body according to this picture:.
Then take a gentle pincer and gently grasp those veins softly, and wipe the blood sometimes after a while until you see the vein has gone from it and the bleeding stops. Take care not to hurt the eye with the edges of the pincer. Do your work halfway through the day in the shade.
And be very steadfast in your work, lest you cut something other than those veins. When you finish, apply the green or red eye salve to the eye, as much as it needs, to consume what remains of the blood. If you are unable to remove all of it at that time, compress the eye with what soothes the pain of the eye.
And leave it for some days until the pain subsides and the swelling recedes. Then do the work again on this condition with the same eye, until this picture of the pincers is freed from it.
And leave it [and the pupil of the one who is being operated on should be in the stone of the apprentice, and the other should dry up the blood, and achieve a view in the front and back of the eye, and you] the original state of the work that the eye opens with fixed or triangular openings, held by the apprentice.
Painful and the pupil of the one who is being operated on should be in the stone of the apprentice, and the other should dry up the blood, and achieve a view in the front and back of the eye, and you by choice start to grasp from above the eye or from below it. The first way is to have two sutures in the upper eyelid, one at the end and the other at the beginning.
And take hold of it between the middle and the corner, then tie a knot from under them. Then take hold of it between the nostril and the cheek, and pull your hand with a light movement until you see that all the vessels have risen. Cut from the smaller western one with pincers or forceps gently.
You are to heal the wound on the arm and to make all ways until it rises above the swelling, but do not cut the flesh, for then tears and blood will flow upon you.
Then cut with the pincers what is above and below the tendons, until there remains only a slight swelling in the armpit. For if you can lift it from the armpit, flay with the wound, this is better, and sometimes it will come away in some people.
And if you cut it, it will swell up for several days, causing pain and inflammation, then attend to it again.
The Nineteenth Section.
On the Return of the Cartilage to the Nose.
Physicians call the cartilage nasura. If they treat it with vinegar or hot medicine as described earlier, and it does not heal, then there is no remedy for it except to incise on the swelling when it hardens and extract all the moisture that is in it or pus.
Until the bone is exposed. If the bone is exposed and you see decay or rottenness, then scrape it with this instrument as follows:.
And it is called the rasor. It is made from Indian steel and its head is rounded like a razor, with an engraving of the cooled or ash-colored metal in fine lines. Then you put it on the spot where the decay is on the bone, then turn it between your fingers as you grip your hand slightly until you feel that decay has been removed.
And do that several times, then press the spot with dried and sticking medicines. If the wound is sealed and the flesh grows in its place, and the flow of pus ceases after forty days, and there is no fresh swelling or event happening in it.
So know that it has healed, and otherwise there is no remedy except to return the cartilage to the nasal orifice in this way, which is to expose the bone again with steel or hot medicine. If the bone is exposed, then take a drill as follows:.
The edge of the chisel will be triangular and its end will be conical, bent towards the side as you see it. Then place it on the bone itself, being that close to the joint and a little further away from the eye. Then bring your hand with the forceps until the bone is pierced and the patient feels it.
That the breath comes out from him if he holds his hand on his nose. Then, when the flesh grows and the place hardens, what was positioned outside will return to the nose, so it will be less painful for the patient, God willing.
The Twentieth Chapter.
Regarding the Return of Sight.
If the eye is opened with its whole contents and there is no defect or diminution in the sight, then the patient should be eased, then freed from the bandage, then have a soft cloth put on the back of the head without any constraint.
Then place on the eye a poultice made of aqua, vinegar, gallnut, and aloeswood. Then tie the eye from above with the compress, using many benefits. The recipe for the benefits is to take a lot of thin sheets, each one folded into four thicknesses, making many of them.
Then place one on top of another as much as the eye needs, then tie it with a strong and thick bandage and repeat the compressing with a soft cloth without constraint. Then remove the compress and leave the eye tied for a day and a night.
If the bandage relaxes during that time, then it should be tightened again. Then remove the bandage after a day and a night as we said. If you see that the eye has returned, but if not, then repeat the compressing, using many benefits, tightening, and compressing until it returns.
The Twenty-First Chapter.
About cutting the tendons.
If a hernia appears in the tendinous layer, then it bulges out and protrudes outside the abdominal walls like a tendinous fold and destroys the appearance of the human body because of this, I wish to cut it as I will describe.
And it is that you insert a needle into the origin of the tendon from below to above, then another needle with a double thread from the opposite side and push it through and leave the first needle as it is.
Then you cut the spot where the double thread is bent, and tie some of the tendon around the needle and pull it tightly then withdraw the needle and apply a wet piece of white linen to the eye until the threads fall off with the tendon then treat the eye as it requires.
Until the wound heals, and the tendon may be tightened from all sides in a circular shape with a piece of cloth until the eye becomes swollen tightly then wrap it with a thin bandage that reaches to the bottom of the eye and the white moisture flows down and subsides then tighten it until it heals.
The 22nd chapter.
In treating a cleft.
This condition which is called a cleft is nothing but a swelling that appears in the eye resembling running water, and the purpose of treatment is for the patient to sit on a raised chair standing upright then take hold of his head with your hands from both sides.
And move it until you see the swelling go down to the bottom of your eye, then stop and do not let it move, and the sight will return and the patient will see things as he used to, and if it does not descend to the bottom as we have mentioned.
And otherwise, have the patient sit in front of you then take a thin bandage and cut it with the ligament above the corneal membrane slightly at the point where the ligament joins the corneal membrane in the eyelid until the matter emerges.
If only a drop of hot water came out of the eye, which has been mixed with opium or water that has been boiled with gall and opium, then it is treated with all other treatments until it clears.
The Twenty-Third Chapter.
We have mentioned the kinds of water in the classification, and which one is suitable for use as a cupping treatment with detailed explanation; then you take it from there according to what is proper. When that happens, the patient should sit before you, elevated opposite the light, near the sun.
And you bind the healthy eye and tighten it well, then raise the eyelid of that eye with your left hand if it is the left eye with water, or with your right hand if it is the right eye.
Then you put the tip of the cupping vessel near the eyelid with a slight inclination towards the smaller corner of the white part of the eye, then push the cupping vessel with force and turn it with your hand until it penetrates into the white part of the eye and feel the cupping vessel that it has reached something hollow.
And it is necessary that the cupping vessel goes as far as the depth of the eye's socket, which is from the white part to the end of the pupil, and the copper will be seen by the observer because of the transparency of the conjunctival mucosa; then the cupping vessel comes out to the top to the position where there is water.
Then you press it downwards once or twice, and if the water comes out from its source, then the patient will see what has opened up before him, and the cupping vessel is in his eye; then he rests a little, and if the water rises, then bring it down again without letting the cup go out.
If it settles and does not rise, then take out the cupping vessel gently with your hand little by little, then dissolve something of pure salt or Andirani in the water and wash the eye from inside; then put on the outside of the eye all of it, whether it is a cloth or a wet cloth.
We bind the white of egg and pure white with it, and then we tie it with the healthy eye. As for us and people of our time, we put on it a tied-up white of egg, in case the hardened one does not permit entry into the eye because some people's eyes are very hard indeed. It is necessary for the surgeon who is called the physician to take this shape:.
Then insert the point only into the severed part, and do not dwell on the puncture, but rather reach for the hardened one in a gentle spot then enter the hardened one as we mentioned, and when you complete your work prepare the patient lying down firmly sleeping on their back in a dark room.
And he abstains from all movements and coughing, and makes his food as natural as possible without stirring his head to the right or left whatsoever, and the bandage remains on him until the third day then remove it in that dark room and try out his sight.
And he will experience things then the bandage returns to the seventh day and it is not necessary to do that during treatment or after the puncture from your time but rather avoid it before the water rises quickly with severe vision.
If a hot tumor appears it is necessary to open the eye before the seventh day and treat that which calms the tumor until it subsides then you can release his sight and place a cloth on his face training his sight from underneath for days while he is in that dark room then.
He exits the room gradually and behaves in his surroundings, and know that the puncture is not sufficient for the learned one without observation repeated times then he proceeds to the work, and I have been told by some Iraqis that they said that he makes in Iraq a wide puncture which absorbs water.
And I have not seen anyone in our land make that nor read it in a book of the early ones and it may be something new, and this is an image of types of punctures for him to stand on its ignorance:.
The manufacture of this instrument is from copper and its tip is made with a special shape like a triangular sharp edge.
Chapter Twenty-Fourth.
In the treatment of flesh that has grown in the nose.
It may grow in the nose various kinds of flesh, some resembling many-legged scorpions, and some being a cancerous tumor turned black, and some being loose and not discolored.
As for the flesh that is not cancerous or malignant, the patient should sit in front of you facing the sun and open their nostrils and receive the forceps into that flesh then pull it out to the outside and cut off what has been grasped with a thin sharp knife from one direction.
Until you are certain that all the flesh has gone, if some remains and you were unable to cut it off, remove it gently with one of the soft instruments until nothing remains; but if blood flows or a hot abscess appears.
So treat it as necessary or if it is one of the malignant tumors, proceed to remove it until the bleeding stops and all the flesh has gone then pour into the nose after cutting some clear water or a drink; but if the nostril opens and moisture flows down to the throat.
So know that it is cured, but if the moisture does not flow as necessary, know that inside there is growing flesh in the upper bones that has not been reached by the cutting instrument, so then you should take a cotton thread with some thickness.
And tie it with many knots and make between each knot a length of a finger or less, and the patient should insert one end of the thread into their nose by force or as much as possible after making it like a needle and pull out his breath until it reaches the turbinate.
The suture will exit from the loop and often behaves like children in a writer's desk, which is an action that makes it easy for whoever wants to do so. Then, both ends of the thread come together, one end coming out of the mouth and the other remaining in the nose.
Then you will use the meat to spread the bond that is in the thread, doing so until you learn that the meat has been cut by the thread bond. Then the thread will come out and become in the nose after wiping away the blood with a gauze that you have soaked in the medicinal solution, doing so for three days or more.
Until the medicinal solution has eaten away all that remains of the meat, then a tube-like thing will remain in the nose for a few days until it heals. If needed, and it has dried out, use it.
And this is an image of the syringe which pours the medicines in the nose:.
He places a bronze or copper like a small candlewick, open-ended and with its channel also.
And if you wish, make the tube closed like a reed, and shape the syringe's nozzle.
It has a handle at its end as you see, used to hold it when the wax or what you want of liquids or flowing things is placed in it.
The 25th Chapter.
In nasal polyps on the tip of the nose.
Many times a polyp grows in the tip of the nose, increases and multiplies with time until its appearance becomes unpleasant.
Therefore, it is necessary to cut it when it first appears and remove the whole of it, then apply a poultice or a cauterizing medication to the site. If cutting fails until it grows large, then look; if it is hard and calcified like a congealed lump with little sensation.
Do not expose it to iron, for it is a cancerous ulcer, and I have often seen cuts made in this ulcer resulting in a great deal of harm to the owner, even if the ulcer is thin-skinned and not inflamed; and I saw that cutting can be done entirely. He should empty the wound and cut it without caution or hesitation, and treat the place with what coagulates and dries until it heals.
The Twenty-Sixth Chapter.
In sewing the nose, lip, and ear. If the connection is severed due to a wound or something similar, know that whenever this happens in one of these facial areas, very little can be done about it except in some people.
When one of those things occurs, look and see if the wound is still bleeding; then gather the edges of the wound together with a suture and treat it until it heals. And if the connection has been severed and each side has become separate, each piece should be peeled away from its visible skin layer until it stops bleeding.
Then gather the two lips together with a suture and tighten it, and apply to it the yolk and gall mixed, and put on top of it a sticking plaster of asphalt or other sticky ointment, and leave it tied for two or three days then release it.
And change the dressing and leave it until the sutures dissolve by themselves, then treat it with ointment until it heals. The method of stitching is to gather the severed connection either with a needle as we described in sewing the abdomen or with thread as I mentioned earlier.
The Twenty-Seventh Chapter.
In removing the swellings that appear on the lips.
Many people may have small, hard swellings inside their lips that resemble some of the seeds of the kirsanah and others smaller or larger, so it is necessary to turn the lip and cut around each swelling and tie it with a thread.
The wound is then cut from all sides, then the place after cutting is filled with powdered gypsum until bleeding stops, and then it is sutured with vinegar, salt, and treated accordingly until the wounds heal.
The Twenty-Eighth Chapter.
About Cutting Excess Flesh in the Gums.
Often a surplus of flesh grows on the gums, which the ancients called Abolos. It is necessary to tie it with a thread or grasp it with forceps and cut it at its origin and let the blood flow, then put powdered gypsum on the place.
or one of the dried and hardened excrescences; if that flesh returns after treatment, often it returns again; cut it off a second time and leave it alone, for it will not return again.
The Twenty-Ninth Chapter.
About Plating the Teeth with Iron.
Matter may accumulate on the surfaces of the teeth from within and without, as well as between the gums, in the form of rough, foul-tasting scales which may spread and become yellowish-green until it reaches the gum and corrupts the teeth because of this.
Then the patient should sit before you with his head in your lap, and you should remove the tartar and tooth that has shown scales to you, down to the very bone, just like you would do with sand, green, yellow, and other colors until it is clean.
And if what is in it does not come out at first, then you should repeat the tartar removal another day and another, until you achieve your goal; and know that the tartar requires a different kind of treatment with many forms and shapes according to what presents itself for your work.
In order that the tartar which is removed from within, is not the same as that which is removed from outside, and that which is removed between the teeth with a different form; and these are many forms of tartar removal, all of which you should have prepared:.
The Thirtieth Chapter.
Extraction of the Teeth.
It is necessary to treat the molar from its pain with all means and not to neglect it, for there is no hope behind if it is extracted; because it is a noble root even if it is not necessary to extract it.
It is necessary if the patient intends to extract it, that you secure until the tooth becomes sound in your hands. For many a time, the patient is deceived by his pain and thinks that it is in the healthy tooth, so he extracts it, then the pain does not depart until the sick tooth is extracted; we have seen this repeated in the actions of barbers.
If the tooth becomes sound in your hands, then it is necessary to wrap around the tooth with a cloth that has some strength until the gum is detached from all sides, then move it slightly with your fingers or with fine forceps gradually little by little until it trembles.
Then you will be able to grasp it with the two big forceps, grasping it well, and the patient's head between your knees as if he had been lifted up not moving then pull out the tooth straight so that it does not break; if it does not come out, else take one of those instruments and insert it under him from all sides gently and gradually move him as you did first.
And if the tooth is perforated or has a cavity, it is necessary to fill that hole with a pledget and seal it well with a thin thread so that it does not open up when you pull on it with forceps; and it is necessary to wrap around the gum from all sides tightly.
And conserve your effort so that it does not break and some of it remains in the patient's mouth causing him a greater pain than his initial one; and beware of doing what foolish barbers do in their bridges and operations without using what we have described.
Many people are afflicted with great pains without their teeth being broken and the roots of some of them remaining intact. Or it is possible that some of the jawbones are removed as we have seen repeatedly, then it is rinsed with wine or vinegar and salt. If bleeding occurs from the site, many times this leads to something like a small abscess forming there.
Unless the abscess is effective, take a caliper that moves the tooth first. This caliper should have long arms and a short handle, thick so it does not bend when you grasp it with the tooth. And this is the appearance of large calipers:.
It should be thick-handed so that even when you grasp it firmly, it does not give way or bend. And let it be made of Indian steel or well-wrought iron, with serrations at the end that fit together, allowing a firm and tight grip.
And the arms can be shaped like a muller so it will also be strong in its grasp.
The twenty-first chapter.
In the removal of tooth roots and the extraction of broken jawbones.
If a root remains when the tooth is extracted that has been broken, it should be placed on the site a piece of fat or ghee for one or two days until the site is softened, then enter with a probe or caliper. which resembles the beak of a bird called balrjaa and this is the appearance of the calipers:.
It should be made like a muller from the inside or like an esculent fork. If it is not possible to extract with these calipers, then you should dig into the root and expose all the flesh with a probe, then enter the instrument which resembles a small awl, this is its appearance:.
Shortening the arm is a little bit thick and should not be pierced lest it breaks. If the origin comes out that way, and otherwise seek assistance with these other tools whose shape is this: the first one has a triangular shape in the part containing some thickness:.

Triangular shape of the curved arm, having some thickness a little lest it breaks, and not to be pierced. Because some diseases have not been mentioned, and the first tools are not available for their diversity, if a bone in the jaw or one of the bones of the mouth breaks or is decayed, then search for it in its place with one of these tools and forceps that were mentioned in the extraction of the origin.
