The 22nd chapter.
On the spreading of bone-setting on other things.
Bone-setting if it grows on something else, disfigures the shape and especially so if that happens in women and children. It is necessary to look at it closely, for if the bone has grown from behind another bone.
If it is not possible to cut off the piece nor break it, then cut it with this instrument which has this shape:.
And it resembles a small Indian file, and let it be made of very sharp-edged iron; the cutting edge should be set at an angle for many days to harden the tooth so as not to loosen other teeth, but if it is possible to break it, then break it with a cold instrument whose shape this is.
It should be all made of India ink and a thin layer of it should be very fine, like the cold instrument with which needles are made; cool the tooth little by little over many days gently, lest the tooth loosen and fall, then trim it afterwards and remove some of its ridges.
And if the tooth has cracked and some of it is causing the tongue to ache when speaking, then one should also cool it until the sharpness of that crack subsides and becomes even and smooth so that it does not cause the tongue to ache nor spoil the speech.
The Thirty-Third Chapter.
In binding moving teeth with silver threads or golden threads.
If the anterior teeth loosen and move as a result of a blow or fall, and the patient is unable to chew on anything that is eaten, lest they fall out, and if treatment with binding agents has not been successful.
The trick in this case is to tie with a golden or silver thread, and gold is better because silver tarnishes and decays after some days, while gold remains as it is forever, not subjecting it to that. And the thread should be of medium thickness in the firmness and thinness according to what suits between the teeth.
The shape of the binding is to take the thread and put it into a curve between the two healthy teeth, then sew with both ends of the thread between the moving teeth, one or more, until the sewing reaches the other side of the healthy tooth.
Then you will return the suturing to its original side and gently pull your thread with wisdom until it does not move at all, and your suture should be near the roots of the teeth so that it does not come undone. Then cut off the excess thread with scissors and join them together and roll them up in a cloth and hide them between the healthy tooth and the mobile tooth.
So that the tongue is not injured, then leave it like this tied up as much as remains, for if it came undone or its tightness was lost, secure it with another thread and enjoy it thus for all eternity. This is an image of teeth and the state of being joined in two healthy teeth and two movable teeth as you see:.
And if one or two teeth fall and come to their place, they will join together as we described and remain, but only a skilled craftsman can do that. And he may take a piece of cow bone and shape it into the form of a tooth and put it in the place from which the tooth fell. And he will tie it as we said, and it will remain and be enjoyed by that.
The 34th Chapter.
In cutting the ligament which appears under the tongue in preventing speech.
This ligament that appears under the tongue may either be natural, born with the human being, or it may be secondary to a wound that has healed.
The procedure for this is to open the patient's mouth and head in your lap, raise his tongue, then cut that nervous ligament with a razor until the tongue is released from its hold. If there is some stiffness and complexity and it was due to the healing of a wound, then insert a hook and split it with a razor until the ligament is severed and the knot is untied.
And beware that the incision is not too deep in the flesh, lest it cuts through a vein and exposes bleeding. Then, mouthwash with rosewater or vinegar and cold water after cutting, then place a cotton thread under the tongue which the patient will hold every night.
Unless it is reformed, do not let the bleeding recur; if bleeding occurs, put powdered gypsum on the place. If the blood overpowers you, apply a compress made of a suitable material to the location. Then treat it with the remaining treatment until it heals.
The 29th Chapter.
Regarding the removal of the toad that has developed under the tongue.
It may happen that under the tongue a tumor resembling a small toad prevents the tongue from performing its natural function, and perhaps even fills the mouth, and in this case one should open the patient's mouth facing the sun and look at the lump.
If you see it is red or black and hard, the patient will not feel its presence; do not meddle with it because it is a tumor. But if it is inclined towards whiteness and there is moisture in it, apply the curette and split it gently with a thin forceps and free it from every direction.
If the blood overpowers you while you are working, put powdered gypsum on it until the bleeding stops then return to your work until you have removed it completely then rinse with vinegar and salt.
Then treat it with the remaining treatment suitable for that, until it heals.
The 38th Chapter.
Regarding the treatment of a tumor of the tonsils.
And whatever grows in the throat from other tumors may develop inside the throat glands resembling those that grow outside and are called tonsils, if treated with what was mentioned in the previous section but did not heal.
And look, if the tumor is hard, red-colored, and insensitive, do not touch it with iron; if it is red-colored and its origin is thick, do not touch it with iron either, fearing bleeding, but rather leave it until it ripens, and then either remove it or let it burst from itself.
If it is white and rounded, and its origin is thin, then this is what should be cut, and the work in it is to look before working if it has settled or reduced some of the abnormality.
Then sit the patient with his face to the sun and his head in your lap, and it will open its mouth and take a servant between your hands and tie his tongue down to the bottom with this instrument:.
You make it from bronze or copper, thin like a scalpel. If you have tied the tongue with this and it becomes clear to you what the tumor is and your sight falls on it, take the forceps and insert them into the abscess and pull them out as much as possible without pulling anything else with them.
Then cut it with this instrument, its shape resembles the pincers except that both ends are bent inwards, very sharply. You make it from Indian steel or Damascus steel:.
If this instrument is not available, then cut it with a chisel, its shape being like this:.
Sharp on one side and not sharp on the other, so after cutting one abscess, cut the other in this same type of cut. Then, after the cut, wash the patient with cold water or vinegar and water.
If blood discharge appears, wash with water that has the shells of almonds or leaves of asafoetida or something similar in it until the bleeding stops then treat him until he recovers. And if tumors appear elsewhere in the throat besides the abscesses, cut them off in the same manner as the cutting of the abscesses whether they be many.
And I treated a woman who had a tumor that had grown inside her throat, hitting the uvula with little sensation, which almost blocked the passage and the woman could not eat or drink water.
The woman was on the verge of death if she had remained for a day or two and the tumor had risen from her nose until it emerged through both nostrils. She then hastened to the physician, who inserted a catheter into one of them, then drew out a healthy piece.
Then she cut it where he reached from the nostril, then did that with what emerged from the other nostril. Then she opened her mouth and pressed her tongue, then inserted the catheter into the same tumor and cut off some of it; there was only a slight bleeding.
Then the woman's throat began to move and she hastened from that moment on to drink water, then regained her appetite; we did not cease cutting off a piece of that tumor repeatedly over a long period of time until it became worn out with us and with her.
Then it was removed and the tumor inside the throat became quiet; it ceased to increase, then it subsided from that direction. I do not know what God did with her afterwards.
The 27th Chapter.
On Cutting a Tumor of the Larynx.
That which is called an "unba" if a discharge descends to the larynx and becomes swollen and white, then it is called an "omda", and if it is thick at the bottom and rounded, then it is called an "unba". If treatment was done as mentioned in the division [of cases] and the treatment did not succeed.
And I saw the hot tumor to have subsided from her, and it was thin; it is necessary to cut it. And if it is not congealed and rounded, nor does it have length, and it is dark red or of a certain color or black, or has no sensation; it is necessary to avoid cutting it.
And there is danger to the patient, so it is necessary if you see her with the characteristics I mentioned from its whiteness and length that you make the patient sit in the shade and press his tongue with the instrument which has been described earlier, then insert the catheter into the tumor.
And pull it down and cut it with one of the two instruments mentioned in cutting the almonds, and you should not cut more than what has increased beyond the natural state without excess, for if you cut more, it will harm the voice and speech.
Then, after cutting it, you use what we described in cutting the almonds and treat it until it heals. If the patient refuses to have it cut, then you should use cunning in persuading him without fear or caution, and the way of persuasion is through sharp medicine, which is that you place the patient's head on your lap.
Then, you tie his tongue with the instrument mentioned earlier. Then, take from the sharp water mentioned in the chapter on binding and mix it with a piece of cloth that has not been washed, making it neither thick nor thin, and fill this instrument with it, like this:.
It should be so that the part you put the medicine on is like the scoop of a spoon, and you put the instrument with the medicine on the same place itself, and the patient lies on his side, so that saliva comes out from inside his throat into this instrument, lest something falls into his throat and harms him.
Then, grasp the medicine with your hand and squeeze it onto the place for about half an hour until you see that it has turned black and the medicine's effect has ceased, and if you want to take a thread, wrap it around the corner of the spoon and soak the thread in the medicine.
And put the thread with the spoon into a tube from above until the thread sticks to the place, do that several times until you achieve what you want from binding, then leave it, for it will dry and fall off after three or four days, if you need to repeat the medicine, make it again.
And after binding, wipe around the place with a thread soaked in ghee and absorb what's left of the medicine. Then, rinse with cold water, treat from outside with bandages and from inside with poultices until it heals, for this type of treatment is more secure than cutting and farther from fear.
And also the lhaaah is treated with what is softer than kai and qatta, it is treated with vinegar on this condition. Fodhainj, zu'uba, sa'tir, sudab, shaykh, babung, qiysuum, and similar herbs are taken, then all or some of them are gathered in a pot and immersed in vinegar.
And it is poured into a pot that has been prepared with the wisdom of the earth, and there will be a hole in the middle of the lid, and an instrument made of tin or bronze is placed on it, like this.
And the end that has the calamus is put into the mouth of the patient until the steam rises to the lhaaah on the instrument, until the lhaaah is satisfied then it is repeated several times until it becomes ripe, and beware not to make this treatment at the first appearance of the tumor.
For it often increases in the tumor, but it should be done when the hot tumor subsides. If this instrument is not available, take a pipe and attach an eggshell to its end so that the patient's mouth does not burn.
Because the shell of the egg prevents the heat of the steam from burning the mouth, and this is one of the good treatments with safety.
The Eighth and Thirty-Ninth Section.
In removing thorns and what sticks in the throat, except for that.

And the patient enters it better because he knows the location of the emerging thing and pushes or pulls his hand with the instrument upwards as much as is necessary until it comes out.
The 39th Chapter.
In the removal of the foreign object in the throat.

He will do that several times and the patient will abstain from water all day, then he will take a cup filled with cold water, open his mouth in it and gargle with it without swallowing any of it and move the water with his hand after a while.
If the leech drops off at the place where it has felt water, then if it does not come out as we have described, it is washed away by urine and by a solution of salt in the instrument which we have mentioned in the book of the Creator; it should be done several times because it will drop off.
The purpose of the instrument in the cauterizer is to take a quantity of hot red wax with fire, and the quantity should be covered by a cloth, except for a hole in the middle. If the leech drops off at the place, then if it does not drop off, the cauterizer should repeat this process and the patient should endure thirst and eat salt and garlic, but should not drink water, for there is no way out except by this method. This is an image of the instrument that attracts the leech from the throat when it has been looked at.

Description of the instrument with which the mouth is opened in this manner exactly.
The Forty-Fourth Section.
He will make a cut in the speech of the boil and split it.
The boils are of many kinds, distinguished according to what is mentioned one by one in this book, and they differ in their contents and nature from two aspects: the type of boil itself and what it contains of moisture.
The second type of tumors that occur in the body because the tumor occurring in the head is not like the tumor occurring in the pelvis, nor is the tumor occurring in a fatty area not like the tumor occurring in a joint for each one of them there is a rule of action.
And among the tumors, there is one that should not be excised until the pus has matured and been fully formed, and there is one that should be excised while it is still fresh and has not yet fully matured, such as those that are close to joints.
Because if the tumor occurs near a joint and persists until it corrupts what is around it, perhaps the ligaments or nerves of that joint will be damaged, becoming the cause of lameness in that limb or making the tumor occur near a main organ.
Because if you delay excision until it has fully matured, you will harm the main organ or make it occur near the pelvis, so you should excise the tumor while still fresh and not yet fully mature, except for the one that occurs near the pelvis, lest the pus spread and perforate into the inside of the pelvis to become an abscess.
And it will become chronic and incurable, and you should learn when to excise tumors that have fully matured, which is at the moment of calm, pain relief, fever abatement, pallor, pulse weakening, and signs of tumor regression.
And you should aim to excise the tumor at its lowest point if possible, so that the bleeding will be towards the bottom or in a more superficial part of the tumor and less severe, and the excision should be in the direction of the length of the body if the tumors are in the hands or feet.
And in the locations of muscles, tendons, nerves, and vessels, and in general in all flat areas without curvature, whereas if it is curved then excise according to that location, and as for tumors occurring in fatty areas, it is best to leave them alone.
Until his vitality becomes stable as we said at the end, you should not cut off excess flesh from him beforehand, for it may cause excessive sweating and many wounds and perhaps harden his lips and nostrils, and some ulcers may break out on the surface of the body in necessity or according to what the affected part needs.
It is necessary to use a small incision in small ulcers and a wide incision or multiple cuts as needed according to the size of the ulcer, and there may be ulcers that require the skin to be slit open and cut if it has become like a shred.
And it was in some cases that the patient died like what is seen in many cases of debility and wasting away, from which some cut a gash with three corners and others cut out something resembling the shape of a palm tree or an Arabian leaf.
And there are those that use a circular incision and a crescent-shaped incision, and so on. As for what does not have a head like smooth flat ulcers, it is necessary to make only a small incision. And if the ulcer is large and has accumulated pus over a long period and been lanced, one should not proceed until all the pus comes out at that time.
But some of it is extracted first, then the ulcer is left until another day and some pus is extracted also, to do that repeatedly by degrees until all of it comes out.
And especially if the patient is weak in strength or a pregnant woman or a young child or an elderly man, the vital spirit often dissolves with the sudden extraction of pus, so that the patient may die and you may not feel it, beware of this matter extremely.
And after lancing these ulcers, it is necessary to clean the wound and examine it. If the ulcer's wound is small or the incision is a single simple one, use the lint of flax or cotton wool. And if the ulcer is large and there are many cuts from lancing,
It is necessary to insert a thread into each seam until some of it reaches the other, and if the tumor has been cut from the skin or scraped off, it should be covered with cotton wool or linen rag without moisture and fastened for three days.
Then remove it and treat it as needed with ointments until it clears, if bleeding occurs during your work use cold water and vinegar after soaking a linen cloth in them and apply it to the bleeding spot several times.
If the bleeding persists, it is necessary to use the remedies and treatments that we have described in many places of this book and in the classification, if you are in the winter season and the location of the tumor is richly supplied with nerves, then anoint the remedies with wine and hot oil.
And apply it to the spot, and if you are in the summer season and the location is hot-blooded, then soak the remedies with water and oil or with wine and oil, all of which should be cold; until the third day as we said, then the tumor will resolve and soften.
And use what is similar to it in its treatment until it clears, this is all you need to know about the treatment of tumors in general; as for the method of detail, I have mentioned each tumor and how to treat it briefly.
The 44th Section.
On the tumors that appear on the skin of the head.
Tumors appear on the skin of the head, small ones that are types of pustules contained within scales resembling chicken pox, and their varieties are many; some are fatty, and some contain moisture similar to pus.
And some contain moisture similar to pus, and some are hard and calcified; all of them have no danger in their incision and removal, unless a blood vessel is encountered when making the incision.
The operation in this case is to incise it first with the instrument which comes after this and is called the madis, until you learn what it contains. If what it contains is moisture, then incise it with a simple incision along this shape:.
Start with an incision from line ~b~ to line ~c~, and if the moisture has been released, cut away the sac that contained that moisture and cut it completely off without leaving any of it at all. For often it recedes if anything remains.
Then soak a thread in the powdered resin, if available; otherwise, in saltwater. Fill the wound with it and leave it for another day, as what remains of the sac will be consumed. Then apply the thread again with the powdered resin twice or thrice if needed.
Until you are certain that nothing remains of the sac, then treat the wound with ointments until it heals. And if the swelling contains fatty matter, incise it along this shape:.
Incise it smoothly and insert the absorbent pads into the edges of the wound, and remove it from all sides. Exhaust your effort in extracting the membrane that contains them, unless a vein intervenes, then do what I described to you afterwards. And similarly, do the same in the swelling if it has become detached from the incision.
And the treatment is as I mentioned, and the incision on the detached swelling is easier because it has little blood and moisture. And some of these swellings that are in the head of some people may not have any moisture with them, which is why I incised a swelling in.
The head of an old woman, and I found the swelling to be as hard as solid stone, white and dense, which no one could break even if they tried to throw it. And what happened with other swellings that occurred in the head was not like this, except for those that appeared on the heads of children.
When dealing with the ears, cut all of them into simple incisions and make the opening from the eardrum so that it is easy to pour in the medication downwards, then treat it according to its condition.
The Forty-Second Chapter.
In the incision on the necks of those that are often exposed to these tumors in the neck and under the armpits and in the groin, and which may appear in every part of the body, some of them being single and others multiple, and some arising from one another.

The Third Forty-Fourth Section.
In a cut of the throat from a tumor that occurs inside the throat.
The ancients have mentioned this cut in the throat and I have not seen anyone in our country perform it, and this is the order of their speech. However, those who suffer from constriction should avoid cutting the throat as it will not benefit them.
In order that all the organs and lung may be at ease, and as for those who have a hot tumor in the mouth or throat or tonsils if there is no cause in the trachea, it is necessary to use the cut in the throat for the relief from the obstruction which arises from constriction.
It is necessary if we wish to do so that we cut the throat under three circles of the trachea or four small cuts in width between two circles as much as the cut is in the peritoneum not in the cartilage and this position agrees with the cut.
Because it is lean of flesh and the blood vessels from it are far away, then if the healer is cautious he should stretch the skin of the throat with a suture, then cut the skin until he comes to the jugular vein, avoiding the blood vessels if he sees anything.
Then he should incise the peritoneum which we have described, and ascertain the incision of the jugular vein from the phlegm that comes out with what is torn off and loss of voice; and leave the wound open for a time until the fear of suffocation has passed. If the time has gone by when he was afraid, he should bring together the lips of the wound from the skin.
And he should draw it alone without a splint, then use the medicines that promote flesh growth until it heals. He who composed this book has said: The explanation of all this talk which we have mentioned is only if they see the patient's windpipe closed by one of these tumors which were mentioned.
And the patient was on the verge of death, and he himself thought to stop breathing. They went up to the incision of the larynx so that the patient could breathe at the site of the wound some breaths and escape from death. But they were ordered to leave the wound open until the disease subsides and its course is three days or so.
So they were ordered to stitch the wound and treat it until it heals, and what I saw with my own eyes was that a servant took a needle and sent it to her throat alone, cut off some part of the pulmonary artery; and I was called to treat her, but found her as if slaughtered, so I uncovered the wound.
I found the blood that came out of the wound to be slight, so I was certain that she had not cut a main artery or a vital one; and the breath was coming out of the wound. So I began by cutting open the wound and treating it until it healed, and nothing was found wrong with the servant except for a slight impairment in her voice, no more.
The wound returned to its best condition after some days, so we say that the incision of the larynx is not dangerous.
The 44th chapter.
In the incision on the tumor that appears in the bronchus from outside and is called the tracheal swelling.

The 45th chapter.
In the incision on types of fatty growths.
Fatty growths are many in kind and I mentioned all their kinds in the division, and it is necessary to inform here about the difference between fatty growths and abscesses as they are confusing, so I say that an abscess has with it heat and fever and frightening pains until the pus subsides. And the abscess continues to grow, and then the fever subsides and the pain ceases, whereas fatty growths are not accompanied by heat or fever or pains, and it is contained in a sac-like casing which has a special cavity for it and it is on the color of the body and it begins like a boil and becomes like a tumor, larger or smaller.
This wound is of two kinds, either fatty or it contains moisture. The colors of the moisture are numerous as mentioned in the classification, therefore if you reach the wound to be treated, first examine and inspect it with the instrument called "al-mads" as its picture appears in the next chapter.
The size of the tumor is then measured, then take out the mads and look at what comes out in its wake. If watery liquid comes out, no matter what color it was, cut it with a slight incision as mentioned in all tumors. And if no liquid comes out after taking out the mads, know that it is fatty.
Cut into it with a well-shaped incision as I have informed you, and attach it to the sutures. Remove the skin from all sides gently and preserve it in a pouch if possible so that you can bring out the tumor correctly with it.
And if the pouch tears while working and you are unable to bring it out correctly, that often happens. Bring it out in pieces until nothing is left. For if anything remains, either little or much, the tumor will return to its original condition.
And if it is difficult and only a small amount remains, then clean the wound with some sharp and effective ointments and compresses. Apply what calms the tumor and treat it with all other treatments until it heals. If the tumor is large, mark its edges and treat it with what brings relief.
And if a vein or an artery obstructs you, or bleeding occurs, immediately apply the powdered powder to the spot and leave it closed for two or three days until the wound heals and the bleeding subsides. Then return to cutting what remains of the tumor.

The 50th chapter.

The 51st chapter.
On cutting of ulcers that occur in the abdomen.
Many people may have some in their abdomens and other parts of their bodies, which are called ulcers because they resemble the fungus, its base is thin and its head is thick. Its edges can become ulcerated and there can be small ones and large ones that are very significant.

And the action in cutting them is to look at them. If the patient is wet and the color of the growth is white, soft and moist, then cut it off with a broad knife and have your assistant hold the cauterizing iron in the fire, as it often happens that much blood flows when they are cut.
Then, if the bleeding is severe, cauterize it. If you see that the patient is becoming anxious and frightened from the cutting with iron, take a strong lead thread and bind it around the growth, leaving it for two days, then increase the tension on the lead, but do not stop tightening it.
Whenever you intervene with the growth until it detaches and falls off on its own without any difficulty, if the growth is thick in origin, there is some fear and danger when cutting it, especially if it is in the abdomen. However, it may be possible to cut half or part of it.
Then, cauterize it so that it does not recur. Then, treat it until the wound heals. And beware of cutting a growth that is cancerous, with little sensation and unpleasant appearance, for it is a type of sarcoma. We will mention sarcoma after this.

If it is due to wind, then its touch is soft, and the treatment in that case is to look. The 31st Section.
For the Removal of Stones in Women.
Only rarely do stones form in women, and if one of them does develop a stone, then it is difficult to treat her and many obstacles arise, for example, the woman may be a virgin, and secondly, you will not find a woman who opens herself up to the doctor.

And in that, there is a risk; if necessity demands it, then you should take a good and experienced female doctor, and rarely are they found. If not, ask for a chaste and companionable doctor, or have a woman present who has some knowledge of this craft regarding women's affairs.

The 70th chapter.
In castration.
That castration is prohibited in our religion.
Therefore, it was not befitting for me to mention it in this book of mine; but I mentioned it for two reasons: one is that if a doctor were asked about it, he should know the treatment for someone who suffered from it, and the other reason is that we often need to castrate some animals for our own benefits.
Like camels, donkeys, cats, and similar animals; so I say that castration is done in two ways: either by emasculation or by cutting. And what is done by emasculation is as follows: we sit the animal in hot water until its femininity subsides, becomes soft and droops.
Then calm it down with your hand until it becomes loose and does not respond to touch. And as for castration by cutting, one should grasp the animal, remove its scrotum with the left hand, then tie up the testicles and cut each one separately.
until the testicles come out, then cut them off after they have been scraped clean, leaving no remaining membranes except for the thin membrane that is on the vessels. This type of castration is better than the one done by emasculation.
Because emasculation may leave some femininity behind, making the animal's intercourse possible, then treat the wound until it heals.
The 60th chapter.
In the treatment of hermaphrodites.
The hermaphrodite is found in men of two types: one where it appears as a kind of space or fold in the scrotal skin, resembling a woman's genital area with hair, and from which urine may flow from what is in the scrotal skin.
And as for women, one type is found and it is located above the vulva on the perineum like a child's genitals in miniature, reaching outside one of them like a man's penis, and the other two like those of females, and the treatment of these three types.
The two types of men and the one type of women should be cut off that excess flesh until its impression is removed, then it should be treated like any other wound until it heals. As for the second type of man from whom urine comes out in the scrotal skin, there is no treatment nor any hope for it.
Chapter Seventy-One.
In cutting off the clitoris and the flesh resulting from the vulva of women.
The clitoris may increase in size beyond the natural order until it becomes ugly and its appearance is repulsive, and in some women it may become so large that it spreads like men's and becomes suitable for coitus.
You should grasp the clitoris with your hand or a forceps and cut it off, without looking at the cutting nor especially at the depth of its origin lest blood flow.
Then treat it like other wounds until it heals, and as for the flesh that grows, it is a flesh that grows in the mouth of the uterus until it fills it.
And perhaps it emerges outside like a tail. Therefore, some people call this disease the "tail-like" illness. It is necessary to cut it off like the clitoris and treat it until it heals.
Chapter Seventy-Two.
In treating stricture.
Stricture is when the woman's vulva is not perforated or the perforation is small, and it is either a natural phenomenon born with it or acquired. The acquired kind is caused by an illness that has progressed, which is excess flesh that has grown.
Fragile or thick, it may be in the depth of the uterus, or on its sides, or above or below it. It prevents coitus and bandaging and childbirth, possibly even menstruation, and recognition of that is by inspection from the woman.
If the blockage is apparent and near, then if it's not apparent, search for it with her fingers or a probe. If the blockage is from a fragile thread and is close to the cervix, begin its cutting by placing something like a sponge on the cervix, then put your little finger from both hands together.
And the woman lies on her back with her legs spread, then stretches the cervix with force until she cuts through the fragile membrane and opens the blockage. Then she takes a piece of cloth, dips it in oil, and puts it on the spot, and has intercourse with the woman every day so that the spot does not become stuck again.
If the membrane is thick and dense, it is necessary to cut it with a broad knife resembling an aspen leaf. If the blockage is from flesh that has grown, tie it off with sutures and cut it off. And have with you medications that stop bleeding without causing harm like calomel, celandine, and lapis lazuli mixed with white of egg.
Then use a wide lead tube so that the wound does not become stuck quickly. Hold it for days and then use a cloth bandage made of dry linen, and treat with all the means of treating an ulcer until it heals. And if there is a growth in the uterus in this form, cut it off in this manner.
Unless it is a cancerous tumor, the cancerous tumor that is in the uterus will not respond to iron at all.

The Sixth and Seventieth Chapter.
On the Delivery of the Dead Fetus.
If you have treated the dead fetus as mentioned in the division of treatment and it has not come out, and necessity compels you to act by hand, then look; if the woman is strong and free from any symptoms that would cause harm, it is necessary for her to lie on a bed on her back.
And her head should be leaning downwards, and her legs lifted high, and a servant should hold her firmly from both sides or tie her to the bed so that her body does not move when the fetus is extracted.
Then he moistens the cervix of her womb with wet cloths, with the juice of the Cynodon dactylon and saponaria, and with the fat of flaxseed. Then he anoints her palms with these cloths and juices. Then she enters the womb gently, then asks for a place where she can grasp the remains of the fetus, and the suitable places for that.
Look, if the fetus is twisted, so that it comes down on its head, then grasp the remains in its eyes or in its shoulders or in its mouth or in its nostrils or beneath its chin or on its scalp or in the nearby places near the ribs or beneath the armpits.

When the fetus' head is in the wrist or elbow, then one should do the same thing in the other hand and legs. If the fetus' head is large and there is pressure on it for exit or water has accumulated in its head, one should insert a sharp forceps between the fingers.

If the head comes out and pressure is applied at the navel, one should cut until the moisture in the chest subsides.
Then the chest will be joined. If it is not joined and there is no exit, cut as much as you can. If it's at the lower abdomen or warm with inflammation, then bind it until the moisture drains from it.
If the fetus is on its legs, then pulling it out and aligning it with the mouth of the uterus is easy. If pressure is applied at the abdomen or chest, then pull it out with a cloth that you have wrapped around your hand and cut open the abdomen or chest until what is inside it drains.
If you have extracted all the organs and pulled out the head, then wait for the placenta to come out. If the mouth of the uterus is open, then enter your left hand into the neck of the uterus, ask for the head with your fingers, and pull it out by the fingers until it reaches the mouth of the uterus, then insert a forceps or two and pull it out with it.
If the mouth of the uterus has become closed and hot, then do not force it, but rather at that time use wet and thick substances to soften it, and use compresses and sit in the waters that have been poured and warmed.
If the fetus is on its side, then if possible, it can be corrected. Otherwise, cut and remove it. Nothing from the placenta should be left inside at all. Once you have finished treating your patient, use what we mentioned earlier for treating hot tumors that occur in the uterus.
If bleeding occurs, then go down into the compressing water and use the rest of the treatment. I have seen a woman who had given birth to a stillborn fetus and then became pregnant with it again.
Then the other fetus died as well. After a long time, an ulcer appeared in her womb and swelled until it burst and started to discharge pus. I was called to treat her and treated her for a long time without the wound healing, so I applied some strong lotion to it.
Then a bone came out from the place, and after some time another bone came out. I was amazed by this because the abdomen is a place where there are no bones, and I thought that it must be from the bones of the deceased fetus. She examined the wound and removed many bones from the skull of the fetus.
And I did not cease to follow this until she removed many bones from her. The woman was in the best of conditions and lived like that for a long time, discharging pus from the place, and that is why I have come here with this rare case.
Because it contains knowledge and assistance for what a physician may attempt to do by hand in treatment.

The 78th chapter.
The extraction of the placenta.
If the placenta is retained after childbirth, then it is necessary for the midwife to grasp herself and then blow on the placenta while pulling your hand on her mouth and nostrils. If it comes out like this, otherwise take a cloth.
And make a hole in the cloth, then put the open herbs like fumitory, senna, dandelion, babbington, and silicified into it. Then soak them in water and carry them to the fire. Then place a silver tube on the hole of the cloth, with one end at the mouth of the uterus.
And hold it until the steam reaches the bottom of the uterus, then breathe as we said. Then the placenta will come out quickly. If it does not come out after this treatment, order the midwife to put her left hand in a mixture of cow's gall or gum arabic.
Then put it into the abdomen and search for the placenta. If she finds it, grasp it and pull it out a little at a time until it comes out. If it is stuck in the depth of the uterus, enter your hand as we described, until you find the placenta, then pull it out gently.
So that the uterus does not fall when pulled strongly, but it is necessary to move it gently to the right and left sides, then increase the pull. Then it will respond and release its attachment. If the mouth of the uterus is constricted, we have described the treatment by blowing, the treatment with the cloth, and the herbs.
If it does not come out with everything we have described, then do not use force on her in the retraction. But it is necessary to bind what has come out to the mouth of the uterus to the woman's thigh, and then anoint it with the quadrangular ointment. It will heal after a few days.
The wound heals and emerges except that if it becomes infected, then a bad odor spreads to the stomach and head and that illness requires suitable smoking.
Therefore, some of the early ones have tried the smoke of herbs and dry trees, the shape of the instrument with which the woman blows when her menstruation and childbirth are delayed and similar things:.
It is made of lead resembling a pipe or it is made of copper, with the thin end in front and the wide end on the fire and the incense is burned until that incense goes away and another one is repeated.
The Seventy-Ninth Chapter.
In the treatment of unruptured hemorrhoids.
Many boys may be born and their hemorrhoids not ruptured, but blocked by a thin membrane, so the wet nurse should pierce that membrane with her finger, otherwise she should bind it tightly with a sharp cloth and warn the muscle not to touch it.
Then she puts a soaked wool cloth on it, in the drink and oil, then treats it with ointments until it heals. If she fears that it will close up, she should put a lead tube into the puncture for many days and remove it when the child wants to have a bowel movement.
And also the constriction of hemorrhoids can occur as a result of wound or abscess, so that constriction should be cut open and then treated with what we mentioned earlier in terms of treatment and medication.
The Eightieth Chapter.
In the treatment of fistulas that occur below.
The fistulas that occur below are a complication and thickening that occurs near the hemorrhoids from outside or in one of the spaces on one side, and there may be one or more fistulas.
If that complication opens up and a watery discharge, white or thin pus, comes out of it, which may be connected to the anus and the rectum, and may not be connected, then the connected one will recognize what comes out of it through bowel movement and flatulence when using the enema.
And perhaps it will emerge from there, and maybe it will be a worm if it is in the pelvis extending to the bladder and to the urethra, or extending to the hip joint and to the coccyx. And what is known as the vermiform appendix extending also to the rectum, but not extending.
That you should put your ring finger into the rectum and insert a thin probe made of copper or iron if there is no obstruction in the vermiform appendix, but if there is an obstruction then put a leaden or horsehair thread into it.
Until you feel the probe or thread in your finger, if you do not feel it at all and nothing comes out of the incision, neither stool nor gas nor worms as we said, then know that it is not extending and hasten to treatment.
And if the vermiform appendix extends to the bladder or to the urethra, its indication is the discharge of urine from it and its refusal to cohere with medicines. And if it extends to the hip joint or to the coccyx, its sign is the reach of the probe to that place.
If there is no obstruction to the bone and there is pain in that direction, and pus constantly comes out of it, and no treatment works nor does it cohere with ointment, and all these extending vermiform appendices are incurable.
And the treatment of it is futile trouble for whoever undertakes it from ignorant physicians. But as for what is not extending and not chronic, one hopes for its cure with iron, as I have described it and tried it, which is to make the patient lie between your hands on his back.
And you should stretch his legs upwards and incline his thighs towards his abdomen, then insert the copper or leaden probe into the vermiform appendix if there is an obstruction in it until you learn where the probe ends. If the patient feels it towards the rectum, then you should put your ring finger into the rectum.
If you feel that the amputated finger has been severed from itself, openly and without any tissue or flesh in between your finger and it, then you should be certain that it is severed and do not bother to reattach it because it will not heal as we mentioned.
And they said that it may heal in some people in rare cases, and with the treatment expected to be beneficial for it, wrap a thin cloth on the stump according to the size of the scrotum as mentioned earlier, and place it inside the scrotum until it reaches the thigh, then repeat it two or three times.
Until you learn that all the excess flesh has been burnt, resembling a bird's quill tube, then treat it with anointed lint in lard until those burnt fleshes emerge, and then treat it with ointment, then he will recover.
And if not, it will never recover with anything else, and as for the severed part, if it did not reach your finger which is in the thigh and there was a thick veil of flesh or tissue between it and the severed part, and you saw the scrotum coming out on the surface of the skin, then cut the skin from the beginning of the scrotum. And you will cut through the skin along with the severed part as it is in the scrotum, until you reach where the end of the severed part ends and the severed part lets go and falls, then clean those excess fleshes resembling a bird's quill tube, leaving nothing behind.
Then treat it with ointment until he recovers, if the bleeding is severe and hinders you from cutting away those fleshes, do your best and hurry to cauterize it with fire or a sharp remedy, for cauterizing with fire gathers two good outcomes, burning that excess flesh.
Cutting the blood and drying out the moisture, then treat it with a poultice of fat or sulfur mixed with oil until the wound becomes inflamed and the burnt flesh emerges. Then treat the wound with salve that is beneficial for solid tissue.
And these medicines have a grip and dryness; if they settle, it is cured and there will be no relapse. If the wound has reached the depth of the ulcer and is away from the surface of the body, then insert your finger into the ulcer and search with it.
If you feel a membrane or a covering of bone or flesh between the edge and the wound, and it is close to the outlet, then there is no way to proceed except through greed and hope. This is by using one of three methods: either to cauterize as we mentioned.
Or else to incise it until you reach its bottom so that you can insert the poultice and treat it from close by, and do not continue to cut lest you cut the surrounding muscle that is around the ulcer, causing stool to exit without control. Then treat it as we mentioned, and perhaps it will be cured as we said.
Or else to pierce that membrane and scrape it after you have incised it close to the ulcer, as we mentioned, either with a scraper or another sharp instrument, then cleanse all the burnt flesh in the incision until you can reach it by searching.
Then fill the entire wound with gauze, including the incision and upper mouth, until it is sealed, leaving the ulcer open inside the ulcer crater, so that it will be less painful for the patient, and sometimes the ulcer may appear in this way.
And when you insert the scraper into the ulcer and it is on one side of the ulcer crater towards the surface of the skin and the edge of the crater, take then a curved scraper like an awl, in this shape:.
And insert into it a slack thread from five threads or approximately that, then insert the retractor by the thread in the navel until it reaches its depth, if it is swollen inside near the seat.
Then withdraw the thread from that hole by inserting your finger in the seat and withdrawing the end of the thread and joining both ends together, tighten them, and leave it for a day or two. Every time you cut the thread in the flesh, tighten it well until those fleshes between the threads fall away, then treat the wound until it heals and closes.
If the navel is not swollen, then push it as far as you can without cutting the muscle lest you cut it. Then do with it as we have mentioned until it heals.
The image of the cauterizing needle that cuts through the navels is such that the cutting part is very sharp and the other side is not sharp, lest it cut what does not need to be cut as you see.
Eighty-first chapter.
In the veins of hemorrhoids which bleed and are cut, and treating fissures.
The hemorrhoids will be in two forms, either they will be inside the seat resembling red pimples or like bunch grapes and they will be small and large and blood will flow from them constantly.
And it will be one and many, and it will be outside the seat at its edges except that those which are outside the seat are in most cases less moist, bleeding yellow water or a little blood constantly, and they will have the same color as the body.
And the treatment for those inside the seat is to order the patient to defecate and strain until the seat comes out and the hemorrhoids appear, then hurry and tie them with thread or grasp them with your finger and cut them at their roots, unless the thread does not hold due to its moisture and relaxation.
Heal it with a rough cloth or a piece of moistened bread or grasp it with your fingers then cut it and leave some sharp ridges on it so that it assumes the shape of the cicatrice or fashion it as mentioned in the chapter on cicatrices.
Then treat it with the remaining treatment until it heals, if the ulcer does not yield to coming out then inject the patient with an injection that is a little bitter to wash away what is in the ulcer and hasten its exit quickly when the patient feels relieved, therefore ease the external ulcers and order them lightly.
And it is that you take it with your fingernails or tie it with a thread and cut it then treat it as we mentioned until it heals, and if he dislikes cutting with iron it is necessary to use his vein in this manner, take a loose string and insert it into the needle.
Then pull the boil upwards and remove it with the needle from its root on the other side, twist the ends of the string below the needle as it is obstructed and tighten the boil tightly then tie the string and withdraw the needle, do that to all the boils and leave one not to be removed.
So that excess blood flows out, then place on the ulcer a soaked cloth in rose water or rose oil and put it on the ulcer and order the patient to remain still, then leave him until the boils drop, if they have dropped treat them with ointments and all the treatment until they heal.
And as for the treatment of fissures, it is often exposed to the roughness of the intestines and stubbornness of nature, so if a medicine does not benefit then it is necessary to scrape it with a scalpel or your fingernails until it becomes soft and sheds its upper crust that prevents union.
Then treat him until he recovers as is fitting, if he does not recover then repeat it with increased severity until his flesh becomes soft and his skin peels, then treat him because he will be cured.
The 82nd chapter.
In the treatment of reversed and unreversed arrow wounds, and of ulcers and boils.
For the arrow wound is a rounded swelling on the surface of the body resembling the head of an arrow, which occurs throughout the body but especially in the soles of the feet and palms of the hands and causes pain when walking.
It is necessary to incise what is around the arrow wound, grasp its point or hook and extract it from its origin, then treat him, and if desired, clean him as mentioned in his section. And as for the dry boils, one of them is a small rough flake lying flat on the surface of the body.
And often it occurs in the hands of children, and its treatment is to swell the boil and cut it or lacerate it with a thread of silk or a hair until it falls off, and if desired, clean it with fire or with a harsh medicine.
And the reversed and unreversed boils can be extracted with the instrument that I mentioned in the treatment of the boil, and as for the boil, it is also a small rough flake lying flat on the surface of the body, going deep into it, and if it is affected by cold, one will find in it a resemblance to the itching of the boil.
And it may occur in the entire body, and most often in the hands. Its treatment is to take a tube from a swan's feather or a strong eagle's feather and shape that tube around the boil until its circular edge is formed, then turn your hand with the tube until you incise what is around the boil.
And make it in the depth of the flesh and extract the boil from its root, and if you wish to do so with a copper or iron tube in this manner.
The tube will be above the armpit, immobile and slightly open, making it easy to control with one's fingers and open or close it as desired.

The 84th Chapter.
In the Treatment of Wounds.
I mentioned in the previous division of treatment that which concerns injuries, and I am referring to its treatment by hand and with medicines on perfection. I say that wounds differ according to what is with the wound and according to where the wound falls.
The things that are with the wounds are many, such as a stone bruise or sword cuts or knife wounds or arrow piercings or stick or spear and so on from many things.
And as for the wounds according to the places of the body, such as a wound that occurs on the head or neck or chest or belly or liver and so on from other organs.
And I will describe the treatment of some wounds to make it a standard and law for all wounds, and I will begin with simple head wounds, especially, because compound ones will be mentioned in the beginning of the third book of this book.
I say: if an injury occurs in the head and it is a simple wound, not a bone fracture, then if it was caused by a stone or something similar and the skin has only been torn and the wound is large and you fear that the patient may develop abscesses, then take a poultice and apply it to the place. And do not delay in doing that and extract blood from him according to his strength, unless a stopper prevents it, especially if the blood emerging from the wound is slight and the stoppage is on the opposite side of the injured part.
And warn the patient against overeating, drinking, and heavy foods, if a stopper prevents bleeding. He should reduce his food intake and not approach meat or drinks containing opium. And apply to the wound a poultice of rose water alone or with opiate drink that contains an equal amount.
And if the abscess is prevented, apply to the wound some of his own blood, as long as it's still fresh and hasn't been exposed to air, like I will describe to you shortly. And if it has been exposed to air, apply some ointments on top of it.
Until the pus discharges, then treat him until he recovers. If the wound is large and caused by a sword or something similar and his lips have not joined together yet, then sew it up as I will describe in sewing abdominal wounds.
If the skin has exposed the bone and attached, but its connection is only slight, then cut it off and treat the wound with medicines that will make the flesh firm again in place of the skin. And instruct the patient to eat foods that contain strength, such as heads and tendons and similar things.
If there is gangrene in the skin and it has not attached to the bone, then cut off all the putrid part and wrap it with something. Then treat the wound. If one of the arteries or veins that supplies blood to the area begins to bleed and the bleeding cannot be stopped by medicines, search for the artery.
If he does not stop bleeding, then let him be treated with a caustic and bind him. If necessity demands it, and what we mentioned does not help, then take away until the blood stops. If these wounds are small and superficial, their treatment is easy and simple, requiring only to sprinkle this powder on them and they will be healed by their own blood.
Before the air changes it, the powder's formula is that one part should be taken from aloes, two parts from wax, and three parts from either unslaked or slaked lime. All of these are to be ground together, sifted, and applied to the wound, tightly bound until a good dressing forms on it.
And it is secured with blood, then bound tightly from above with bandages and left undisturbed until it ceases to bleed. For as long as it continues to ooze, the treatment will not be effective; but if lime alone is available, that can be used instead, should aloes and wax not be at hand.
And this action can also be performed with vinegar in many large wounds, if it is applied to them and bound tightly, and the wounds are still bleeding freely from their own blood, without being affected by air. However, if air has had some effect on them, especially during the summer time.
There is no meaning in applying this powder as mentioned earlier, except to let it be covered with some ointment or a poultice made from barley flour mixed with water and honey until the pus forms, then treat it with the rest of the treatment until it heals.
As for the fracture of the bone near the wound, if it is slight, pull it out with a piece of leather. I have mentioned the treatment for head fractures in what remains to be discussed regarding neck surgery; and if the wound is in the neck, there will be no difference in the treatment between this and a simple head wound.
If he has cut a cord from the neck or an artery, then if it is a cord, there is no remedy except to avoid treating it with compression like a vice or a tourniquet and similar things because they harm the nerve and tear it.
And nothing cold should be placed on the wound whatsoever, because the essence of the nerve is cold and its connection to the brain which is the noblest of organs will be affected. What he uses to treat it from medicinal substances like camomile washed with sweet water, repeatedly anointed with oil or with rose ointment and tamarind.
If it is also washed with sweet water and all the metallic stones in this condition, and soft ointments. And if the wound is large, then use suturing or bring his lips together with thread, then treat it until it heals.
If the wound has a hollow and in its bottom, pus has accumulated and is flowing into it. If an artery has been cut in the wound and blood begins to flow, stop it or tie it off or compress it if necessity demands that.
If the wound has cut some or all of the tracheal rings and the ligaments have relaxed, gather up the skin flaps with suturing to a ring-shaped piece of the trachea, do not touch the trachea but smooth it out and put it back in its natural shape then tighten it tightly and leave it for days.
Then treat it with ointments that contain astringent and drying properties until it heals. If the wound has affected the bone, open it up. If there are fragments of bone, extract all or as much as possible of what you can and leave the rest alone until the wound has healed and eased, making it easier to remove.
If the wound is fresh, apply to it the powder that we have described. If bone has been exposed in the wound and has become inflamed, treat it as will be mentioned in its place in thoracic surgery and between the shoulders.
If the wound is from a spear or knife and you see it has pus, then look; if wind comes out of it when the patient breathes, know that it's a battle wound. If not, and it's fresh with her blood, do not put in the first instance herbs nor draw it, lest the blood stagnate in its pus.
He will relapse to the heart and kill the patient. But put in it a poultice that is attractive, and leave it on during the day twice. If you do not have a poultice, put into the mouth of the wound a good cotton cloth to absorb what comes out from the moisture, and let the patient's sleep be on the wound.
There is no need for what gathers in it. And if the wound has been three days or more, and there is neither convulsion nor fainting, nor oppression of the breath, and you see all his conditions are good, know that the wound is healed, and use lint and other treatment until he recovers.
If purulence persists and the stench is always present, know that it has become gangrenous, and treat it from its source. The patient on the wound is not as I described earlier, but if the wound is in the chest or back, treat it as mentioned earlier with suturing.
If it is large or with ulcers, and if it is small, if it has affected the bone and cut out fragments from it, then search the wound and begin to remove those fragments if they are clean. If not, leave them until.
The wound will soften and make it easier to remove them. As for other wounds that occur in all organs, the treatment of them is as we mentioned earlier.
Fifth Section Eighty-Nine.
In wounds of the abdomen and rectal discharge, and sewing it up.
The wound that is exposed to the abdomen can be large or small or medium-sized. The large one may discharge intestines or several intestines, and its introduction and sewing up are harder and more difficult.
The small hernia is also difficult from another aspect, so it is necessary that its reduction be more difficult and the intestine not advance in entering its place except at its hour, it becomes swollen and thick, making its entrance difficult. Therefore, the best hernias are the medium ones because they do not make the intestine's reduction as difficult as these two types.
Know that stitching the abdomen is on four sides, two of which are common to stitching the abdomen and other surgeries of the body, while the other two are special for stitching the abdomen only.
And I describe it to you one by one with explanation and clarification, so I say: if the wound is small and something from the intestine has come out and its return is difficult, this is due to one of two reasons: either because of the smallness of the hernia as we said, or because the intestine is obstructed in advance by the contraction of air.
So if that is the case, it is necessary to soften it by dipping a sponge or wet cloth in lukewarm water and adding asafoetida and cumin, and then wrap the intestine with it until the obstruction is released.
And it can also be done with the decoction of the herb that contains aloes, and this is better than water alone in releasing the obstruction. If you see the obstruction has released, then put the intestine in a lukewarm bath made from cumin or baker's yeast, and it will slide into its place with ease.
And if it still does not return after this treatment, then split the hernia a little with the instrument used to cut fibers and the first treatment is better than splitting, but only requires splitting when necessary and all other means have failed. This is an image of the instrument:.
Its direction is one-way, limited in one direction and unlimited in the other, and the thin end does not become as sharp as a scalpel but is slightly flared, and it is an instrument similar to a small saw as you see. If the wound opens up and the intestine enters, then its return should be on its natural shape.
If you can manage that, it is better. But if the wound is wide and in the lower abdomen, the patient should lie on his back and lift his legs higher than his head. If it is in the upper abdomen, he should lift his head and chest higher than his belly.
And likewise, if the wound is in one side of the abdomen, always make sure that the side where the surgery is to be performed is higher than the other side. Thus, it should be done in great operations and middle-sized ones.
And as for small operations, do what you can and then prepare before you a faithful servant to hold the wound in his hands, gather its edges together, and uncover it little by little for the one doing the suturing.
And this is the general method of suturing, which is to take a needle or several needles according to the size of the wound, then leave a part of the wound as thick as the nail and insert one needle without entering it into the edges of the skin. With the edges of theomentum underneath the skin from inside, until it is inserted from that side, and having brought together the edges of the skin and theomentum, so that there are four layers. Then tie with a double thread around the needle on both sides, until the edges of the wound come together firmly.
Then leave a part as thick as the finger also and insert another needle, then tie it with the thread like you did with the first needle, and continue to do that as many times as you need needles until you have completely covered the wound, and let the needles be intermediate between thickness and thinness.
Because very thin needles are quickly cut through the flesh and also hard to enter the skin, so it is necessary for them to be intermediate in thickness and thinness. And one should not insert the needle into the edge of the skin too closely.
Unless the flesh is torn off quickly and the wound is not sutured before, nor should it be far from suturing lest the wound prevent healing. Then cut off the tips of the needles so that they do not hurt the patient when he sleeps and make for him a support from torn cloth from every side to hold the tips of the needles.
And leave it until you learn that the wound has healed, and this type of suture with needles is thus more suitable for small wounds because it can be sufficient to suture it with one or two or so needles.
Or the method of suturing for a second ordinary case is that you gather all four layers, namely the skin and the peritoneum, in one shot with a needle having a thread of moderate thickness and roughness, then if this is completed with the needle, you remove it from the side where you started it.
So that the thread is knotted from above the wound, to make the suturing like the way of sewing with silk threads which tie things together and leave a small thickness between each stitch, and this type of suturing is known to everyone.
And with this suturing, I have sewn up a surgery that was presented to a man in his stomach, who had been injured by a knife, and the wound was more than a span long and he had come out from his bed about two spans from the middle of his bed, and the wound was in the middle of the abdomen.
Then I waited for him to recover from his bed outside the wound for twenty-four hours, and the wound healed in about fifteen days, and I treated him until he recovered and lived for many years afterwards, managing all his affairs, and doctors would say that he would never recover at all.
And it is a wonder that I did not treat him with ointment because I was in a place where there was nothing of medicine, so I would put two layers of gauze on the wound during the day and entrusted its cleaning to honey water until he recovered.
And as for one of the specific types of suturing, I mention what Galen said, that is to start the suturing from the skin and insert the needle from outside to inside. If the needle penetrates the skin and muscle, then it should proceed in a straight line throughout the entire abdomen.
I left the edge of theomentum on the side where I inserted the needle and penetrated it, then inserted the needle in its other edge from inside to outside on the other edge of theomentum. Then, if I had penetrated it, I would penetrate it again in this same edge from outside to inside.
And leave the edge of theomentum on this side, then insert the needle in its other edge from inside to outside and insert with it into the peritoneum until you reach its edge.
Then, start again from this same side and tie with the edge that is from the peritoneum on the other side, and withdraw the needle from the skin that is near it, then insert it back into that skin and tie the edge of theomentum that is on the other side with this edge of theomentum.
And withdraw it from the skin that is near it, and do that again and again until you have sewn all the incision on this pattern, and in general, this suturing method is called the suture of the frasers for the fur.
That is, to sew the peritoneum once on one side with the edge of the skin and leave it once on the other side until you are finished, and as for the second specific type of suturing mentioned by Galen, this is his word exactly.
And it is that you sew it on the pattern that some practitioners of medicine sew, by joining each part to its corresponding counterpart in a natural manner, by attaching the edge of theomentum to its other edge and the edge of the peritoneum to its other edge, as I have described to you.
The needle should be inserted in the peritoneal fold, which is near you from outside and penetrate it into the inside alone, leaving the peritoneum intact. Then the needle should be withdrawn and reinserted from outside to penetrate both peritoneal folds, and then also withdraw it again.
It should be inserted from the inside to the outside in the other peritoneal fold, which is on the opposite side. And this stitch of suturing is better than the common easy suture mentioned earlier, as Galen has written. Some have said that the abdomen can be stitched with two needles. And that is by inserting one thread into both, starting by introducing the needle from your side and piercing it to the other side, then introducing the other needle from the opposite side of it and piercing it from your side according to the stitching of the scaphoids whether.
Know that the rupture in the middle of the abdomen is harder to suture than in any other place in the abdomen. And as for treating the wound, its rule is like that of all wounds, namely: if you have recognized the wound fresh with blood before the air has changed it and have washed it and marked it out and made it neat, then apply the medicinal powder.
If the wound has been changed by air, then apply some ointments that will help it until it heals and the stitches fall away and the peritoneum and folds are reunited, then treat it as you would any other wound until it is healed.
If you don't have medicines, apply the cotton lint as it begins to heal, and change it twice a day as I have taught you, until it is healed. For in most cases, if the wounds are simple, you won't need any further treatment, unless you fear that the wound may affect the main organs with pain.
It is necessary to soak a linen cloth in moderate heat oil or rose fat and place it around the areas between the armpits and groin, if he feels pain or odor in his stitches then very often this is cured by drinking black vinegar water.
And especially if the odor has spread to his stitches and become a gaping wound in his belly, know that what is thick from the intestines is easier to heal, and what is thin is harder to heal.
And as for the sigmoid colon, it does not accept healing from surgery at all, due to the abundance of its blood vessels and their thickness, and the delicacy of its lining and proximity to the nature of the nerve. The 68th chapter.
In treating catarrh and nasal ulcers.

He is on the truth, tangled in a hard white bone, with no pain accompanying it, having a cavity like the hollow of a bird's wing.

And I have mentioned in the classification when mentioning wounds that not every ulcer heals or puts on good flesh, and it is due to one of nine reasons, either due to lack of blood in the body, or its coagulation, or because there is hard flesh within it and on its edges preventing the growth of good flesh.
